      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>, <b>New Year's Eve</b> (also known as <b>Old Year's Day</b> or <b><a href="/wiki/Saint_Sylvester%27s_Day" title="Saint Sylvester's Day">Saint Sylvester's Day</a></b> in many countries), the last day of the year, is on <a href="/wiki/December_31" title="December 31">31 December</a>. In many countries, New Year's Eve is celebrated at evening <a href="/wiki/Party" title="Party">parties</a>, where many people dance, eat, drink, and watch or light fireworks. Some <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> attend a <a href="/wiki/Watchnight_service" title="Watchnight service">watchnight service</a>. The celebrations generally go on past midnight into <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/January_1" title="January 1">1 January</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a>, are examples of the first places to welcome the New Year, while <a href="/wiki/Baker_Island" title="Baker Island">Baker Island</a> (an uninhabited atoll part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands" title="United States Minor Outlying Islands">United States Minor Outlying Islands</a>) and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> are among the last.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png/220px-Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png/330px-Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png/440px-Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="882"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_that_do_not_celebrate_New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day_on_1st_January.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Countries where the main celebrations of the New Year are other day than on 1st January
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, many people celebrate New Year's Eve by going to church; others go to nightclubs, pubs or take to the streets to celebrate. At midnight, fireworks are displayed across various cities of Ghana, especially in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tema" title="Tema">Tema</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">Nigeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Nigeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg/220px-Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg/330px-Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg/440px-Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Artiste_Davido_entertaining_the_crowd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>HKN's <a href="/wiki/Davido" title="Davido">Davido</a> entertaining the crowd at the <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Countdown" title="Lagos Countdown">Lagos Countdown</a> 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, the New Year's Eve is often celebrated by going to church; others go to nightclubs, and parties organised by individuals, communities or State government like the <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Countdown" title="Lagos Countdown">Lagos Countdown</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Countdown" title="Lagos Countdown">Lagos Countdown</a> is an event in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, created to increase tourism and making Lagos a premium destination for business and leisure. The event kicks off in December and lasts till 1 January. It is attended by an average of 100,000 people. The event takes place at the <a href="/wiki/Eko_Atlantic" title="Eko Atlantic">Eko Atlantic</a> city, beside the Barbeach attracting thousands of domestic and foreign tourists who are entertained every evening by different artists. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rwanda">Rwanda<span class="anchor" id="Rwanda"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rwanda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, New Year's Eve is celebrated mostly by going to church, taking part in social gatherings and family activities. The services usually start from 6<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm for the Roman Catholic church and 10<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm for the Protestants. At 00:00, the president delivers an end-of-year address which is broadcast live on many Radio and Televisions stations.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Fireworks were introduced in recent years, with the most significant displays happening at <a href="/wiki/Kigali_Convention_Centre" title="Kigali Convention Centre">Kigali Convention Centre</a>, Rebero Hill, Mount Kigali. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>People in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> vote on a top ten music countdown before 31 December. When the countdown reaches number one, the song with the most votes plays on all the country's radio stations. Fireworks are lit all around South Africa. People engage in occasional drinking and braais. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Sudan">South Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: South Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, people attend church services at many churches in Juba. The service begins at 9<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm. At the stroke of midnight, people sing the famous <a href="/wiki/Christmas_carol" title="Christmas carol">carol</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Hark!_The_Herald_Angels_Sing" title="Hark! The Herald Angels Sing">Hark! The Herald Angels Sing</a>" to mark the end and beginning of the year with a blessing. The service ends at 12:30<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas"><span class="anchor" id="Celebrations"></span>Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG/220px-Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG/330px-Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG/440px-Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1608"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Quemamu%C3%B1ecoLP01despues.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The burning of dolls is a local tradition in the city of <a href="/wiki/La_Plata" title="La Plata">La Plata</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> include a family dinner of traditional dishes, including <i><a href="/wiki/Vitello_tonnato" title="Vitello tonnato">vitel tonné</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">asado</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sandwiches_de_miga" title="Sandwiches de miga">sandwiches de miga</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pionono" title="Pionono">piononos</a></i>. Like dessert: <i><a href="/wiki/Turr%C3%B3n" title="Turrón">turrón</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mantecol" title="Mantecol">mantecol</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Mexican_dishes#Desserts_and_sweets" title="List of Mexican dishes">pan dulce</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Just before midnight, people flock to the streets to enjoy fireworks and light firecrackers. The fireworks can be seen in any terrace. The first day of the New Year is celebrated at midnight with cider or champagne. People wish each other a happy New Year, and sometimes share a toast with neighbours. Parties often continue until dawn. Residents in <a href="/wiki/La_Plata" title="La Plata">La Plata</a> have a long tradition making giants dolls, mostly made of paper and wood with some fireworks on it, to later on after the midnight burn them down.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The celebration is during the summer, like in many South American countries, so it's normal to see many families in the New Year at tourist centers of the Argentine Atlantic coast (<a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Necochea" title="Necochea">Necochea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villa_Gesell" title="Villa Gesell">Villa Gesell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miramar,_Buenos_Aires_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Miramar, Buenos Aires Province">Miramar</a>, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Feliz_2013_(8332275903).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg/220px-Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg/330px-Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg/440px-Feliz_2013_%288332275903%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3806" data-file-height="2262"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Feliz_2013_(8332275903).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Copacabana_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Copacabana (Rio de Janeiro)">Copacabana</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> hosts one of the world's largest fireworks displays on New Year's Eve, attracting millions of spectators.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Brazil, New Year's Eve (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Ano Novo</i>) is typically celebrated at large parties hosted by restaurants and clubs; local traditions determine who opens a bottle of <a href="/wiki/Champagne_(wine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Champagne (wine)">Champagne</a> at midnight. People often wear colors with religious symbolism on New Year's Eve, such as white for good luck, yellow for good energies, happiness and money, red for love). Rituals such as the consumption of grapes, lychees and lentils also take place due to this mixture.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most prominent public celebration in Brazil is a fireworks display on <a href="/wiki/Copacabana,_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Copacabana, Rio de Janeiro">Copacabana Beach</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, which is one of the world's largest. In 2017, it was estimated that the fireworks would attract over three million spectators to welcome 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> On television, the most prominent New Year's Eve special is <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a>'s <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Show_da_Virada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Show da Virada (page does not exist)">Show da Virada</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Show_da_Virada" class="extiw" title="pt:Show da Virada">pt</a>]</span></i>, which features a concert filmed from a different Brazilian city annually, and live segments carrying coverage of the celebrations <sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The capital city of <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a> holds a public celebration on the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Monumental Axis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_Man%C3%A9_Garrincha" title="Estádio Nacional Mané Garrincha">Estádio Nacional Mané Garrincha</a>. Celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a> are centred upon a fireworks display on the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Negro_Bridge" title="Rio Negro Bridge">Rio Negro Bridge</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> hosts the main celebration in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="São Paulo (city)">São Paulo</a>, Brazil's largest city.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another notable New Year's Eve tradition in São Paulo is the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Silvester_Road_Race" title="Saint Silvester Road Race">Saint Silvester Road Race</a>, which has been held annually since 1925, and is currently held as a <a href="/wiki/15K_run" title="15K run">15K run</a> through the city's <a href="/wiki/Central_Zone_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Central Zone of São Paulo">Central Zone</a>. The route features several major streets and landmarks, including the <a href="/wiki/Viaduto_do_Ch%C3%A1" title="Viaduto do Chá">Viaduto do Chá</a> and Paulista Avenue.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve traditions and celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> vary regionally, but are typically similar to those in the United States, with a focus on social gatherings and public celebrations (such as concerts and fireworks displays).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1992, the sketch comedy troupe <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Farce" title="Royal Canadian Air Farce">Royal Canadian Air Farce</a> began airing an annual New Year's Eve special — <i>Year of the Farce</i> — on <a href="/wiki/CBC_Television" title="CBC Television">CBC Television</a>, which featured sketches lampooning the major events and news stories of the year. The 1992 edition was presented as a one-off special (as the troupe's first production made specifically for television), and became part of a regular <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Farce_(TV_series)" title="Royal Canadian Air Farce (TV series)"><i>Royal Canadian Air Farce</i> television series</a> that aired from 1993 through 2008. The 2008 edition doubled as the program's <a href="/wiki/Series_finale" title="Series finale">series finale</a>, but <i>Year of the Farce</i> continued to air as an annual reunion special until 2019, featuring members of the original cast.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sun-farcenye_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sun-farcenye-19">[19]</a></sup> It was announced that due to budget cuts and other factors, the 2019 edition (which premiered prior to New Year's Eve) would be the final edition.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2017 (with the inaugural edition marking the beginning of the country's <a href="/wiki/150th_anniversary_of_Canada" title="150th anniversary of Canada">sesquicentennial</a> year),<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> CBC has also broadcast a more traditional countdown special, with music performances and live coverage of festivities from a city in each <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Canada" title="Time in Canada">time zone</a> (with the telecasts split regionally across the CBC's regional stations).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Similarly, the CBC's <a href="/wiki/French-language" class="mw-redirect" title="French-language">French-language</a> television network <a href="/wiki/Ici_Radio-Canada_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Ici Radio-Canada Télé">Ici Radio-Canada Télé</a> airs its own New Year's Eve comedy special, <i><a href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_(TV_series)" title="Bye Bye (TV series)">Bye Bye</a></i>. Unlike <i>Year of the Farce</i>, <i>Bye Bye</i> has been presented by various comedians; originally running from 1968 to 1998, it was revived in 2006 by the Québécois troupe <a href="/wiki/Rock_et_Belles_Oreilles" title="Rock et Belles Oreilles">Rock et Belles Oreilles</a>. Its 2008 edition, hosted and co-produced by Québécois television personality <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9ronique_Cloutier" title="Véronique Cloutier">Véronique Cloutier</a>, was criticized for featuring sketches that viewers perceived as offensive, including sketches making fun of English Canadians and American <a href="/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States" title="President-elect of the United States">president-elect</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 2018, the special was seen by 3.3 million viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Canada_men%27s_national_junior_ice_hockey_team" title="Canada men's national junior ice hockey team">Canada men's national junior ice hockey team</a> usually plays their final preliminary round game at the <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_U20_Championship" title="IIHF World U20 Championship">IIHF World Junior Hockey Championship</a> on New Year's Eve.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Team_Canada_New_Year%27s_Eve_Game" title="Team Canada New Year's Eve Game">The game</a> typically has millions of viewers on <a href="/wiki/The_Sports_Network" title="The Sports Network">TSN</a> and attracts sellout crowds when the tournament is played in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg/220px-A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg/330px-A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg/440px-A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%B1o_Nuevo_Vi%C3%B1a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Over one million visitors crowd the streets and beaches of <a href="/wiki/Valparaiso" class="mw-redirect" title="Valparaiso">Valparaiso</a> each New Year's Eve.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New Year's Eve is celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> by the observation of traditional rituals, such as wearing yellow underwear and yellow clothing. It is said to restore vitality to your life. People who want to travel walk the streets with a suitcase in hand, others hold money in their hand or place coins at their door for good fortune in the new year. Celebrations include a family dinner with special dishes, usually lentils for good luck, and twelve grapes to symbolize wishes for each month of the coming year.<sup id="cite_ref-Chile_traditions_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chile_traditions-27">[27]</a></sup> Family celebrations usually last until midnight, then some continue partying with friends until dawn. In Chile's capital <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a>, thousands of people gather at the <a href="/wiki/Entel_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Entel Tower">Entel Tower</a> to watch the countdown to midnight and a fireworks display.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are several fireworks shows across the country. Over one million spectators attend the most popular, the "Año Nuevo en el Mar", in <a href="/wiki/Valparaiso" class="mw-redirect" title="Valparaiso">Valparaiso</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Since 2000, the sale of fireworks to individuals has been illegal,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> meaning fireworks can now only be observed at major displays. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> it is a traditional celebration. There are many traditions across the country. Included among these traditions are: a family dinner with special dishes, fireworks, popular music, wearing special or new clothes, eating empanadas and different parties. With each stroke of the clock until midnight, the families eat grapes. In Colombia is common to use more than one tropical substances. It is past of the culture. Other types of fruits are: Mellon, sandia, or watermelon and chontaduro<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Costa_Rica">Costa Rica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Costa Rica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, families usually gather around 8<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm for parties that last until 1 or 2<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am, the next day. There are several traditions among Costa Rican families, including eating 12 grapes representing 12 wishes for the new year, and running across the street with luggage to bring new trips and adventures in the upcoming year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador">Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ecuador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A New Year's Eve tradition in <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> is for men to dress haphazardly in drag (clowny looking make-up, cheap colorful wigs, very hairy legs in miniskirts) for New Year's Eve representing the "widow" of the year that has passed. The "widows" then go to the streets and stop each car that passes on that particular street in order to parody some form of sexy dancing. Large crowds would gather around to watch and laugh at the entertainment and the drivers are forced to give the "widows" some coins in order to obtain passage through the street.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are also traditional family events, meals, and modern celebrations such as hosting parties and going to nightclubs. People usually eat grapes and drink Champagne with close family members and friends.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Salvador">El Salvador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: El Salvador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, New Year's Eve is spent with families. Family parties start around 5:00<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm, and last until 1:00 to 3:00<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am, the following day. Families eat dinner together and sing traditional New Year's Eve songs, such as "Cinco para las Doce". After the dinner, individuals light fireworks and continue partying outside. A radio station broadcasts a countdown to midnight. When the clock strikes midnight, fireworks are lit across the country. People start exchanging hugs and wishes for the new year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The main event takes place at midnight where fireworks are lit along with thousands of life-size effigies called "Año Viejo". Most every local family creates the effigy from paper scraps, old clothes or purchases it altogether. They place just outside the front of their home. The effigy represents things you disliked from the previous year and are made to look like famous celebrities, politicians, public servants, cartoons, etc. They are burnt right at midnight to shed the old year and represent a new beginning. Some of the braver Ecuadorians jump through these burning effigies 12 times to represent a wish for every month.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guatemala">Guatemala</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Guatemala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, banks close on New Year's Eve, and businesses close at noon.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In the town of <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Guatemala" title="Antigua Guatemala">Antigua</a>, people usually gather at the Santa Catalina Clock Arch to celebrate New Year's Eve (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Fin del Año</i>). In <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a> the celebrations are centered on Plaza Mayor. Firecrackers are lit starting at sundown, continuing without interruption into the night. Guatemalans wear new clothes for good fortune and eat a grape with each of the twelve chimes of the bell during the New Year countdown, while making a wish with each one.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The celebrations include religious themes which may be either <a href="/wiki/Maya_mythology" title="Maya mythology">Mayan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Catholic celebrations are similar to those at Christmas. Gifts are left under the tree on Christmas morning by the Christ Child for the children, but parents and adults do not exchange gifts until New Year's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Mexicans celebrate New Year's Eve, (Spanish: <i>Vispera de Año Nuevo</i>) by eating a grape with each of the twelve chimes of a clock's bell during the midnight countdown, while making a wish with each one. Mexican families decorate homes and parties in colors that represent wishes for the upcoming year: red encourages an overall improvement of lifestyle and love, yellow encourages blessings of improved employment conditions, green for improved financial circumstances, and white for improved health. Mexican sweet bread is baked with a coin or charm hidden in the dough. When the bread is served, the recipient of the slice with the coin or charm is said to be blessed with good luck in the New Year. Another tradition is to make a list of all the bad or unhappy events over the past 12 months; before midnight, this list is thrown into a fire, symbolizing the removal of negative energy from the new year.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> At the same time, they are expressed for all the good things during the year that is ending so that they will continue in the new year.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mexicans celebrate with a late-night dinner with their families, the traditional meal being turkey or pork loin. Afterwards many people attend parties outside the home, for example, in night clubs. In <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> there is a street festival on New Year's Eve centered on the <a href="/wiki/Zocalo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zocalo">Zocalo</a>, the city's main square.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Celebrations include firecrackers, fireworks and sparklers and shouts of "¡Feliz Año Nuevo!"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama">Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>For New Year's Eve, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> usually celebrates with a dinner, followed by multiple individual fireworks celebrations. Fireworks begin around 11<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm for parties that last until 1 <span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am, the next day. Many leave the city and go to the rural towns across the country, to celebrate with family and friends. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suriname">Suriname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Suriname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>During New Year's Eve in <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, the Surinamese population goes into cities' commercial districts to watch fireworks shows. This is a spectacle based on the famous red-firecracker-ribbons. The bigger stores invest in these firecrackers and display them in the streets. Every year the length of them is compared, and high praises are held for the company that has managed to import the largest ribbon. These celebrations start at 10<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am and finish the next day. The day is usually filled with laughter, dance, music, and drinking. When the night starts, the big street parties are already at full capacity. The most popular fiesta is the one that is held at café 't Vat in the main tourist district. The parties stop between 10 and 11<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm after which the people go home to light their <i>pagaras</i> (red-firecracker-ribbons) at midnight. After midnight, the parties continue and the streets fill again until daybreak.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a> the tradition is to celebrate in one's yard with friends, family and neighbors, and eat and drink till sunrise. At midnight the city becomes festive with fireworks in every direction. The celebration only starts at midnight. Music is heard from all the houses and bars, nightclubs, street parties, and Soca raves. The people are celebrating not only the new year but the beginning of the carnival season as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_(9234114888).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg/275px-Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="275" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg/413px-Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg/550px-Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_%289234114888%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1366"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Working_New_Years_Eve_Social_Media_for_NBC_(9234114888).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A crowd gathered in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a> at midnight during its annual "<a href="/wiki/Times_Square_Ball" title="Times Square Ball">ball drop</a>".
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the United States, New Year's Eve is celebrated with formal parties and concerts, family-oriented activities, and large public events such as firework shows and "<a href="/wiki/List_of_objects_dropped_on_New_Year%27s_Eve" title="List of objects dropped on New Year's Eve">drops</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most prominent celebration in the country is the "<a href="/wiki/Times_Square_Ball" title="Times Square Ball">ball drop</a>" held at <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, which was inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Time_ball" title="Time ball">time balls</a> that were formerly used as a <a href="/wiki/Time_signal" title="Time signal">time signal</a>. At 11:59:00&nbsp;p.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">ET</a>, an 5,400-kilogram (11,875&nbsp;lb), 3.7-metre-diameter (12&nbsp;ft) ball is lowered down a 21-metre-high (70&nbsp;ft) pole on the roof of <a href="/wiki/One_Times_Square" title="One Times Square">One Times Square</a>, reaching the roof of the building sixty seconds later. The event has been held since 1907, and has seen an average attendance of one million spectators yearly. Since 2009, the ball itself—which is adorned with <a href="/wiki/Waterford_Crystal" title="Waterford Crystal">Waterford Crystal</a> panels and an LED lighting system—has been displayed atop the building year-round.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-deconstructed_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-deconstructed-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn-Green_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-Green-39">[39]</a></sup> The spectacle has inspired <a href="/wiki/List_of_objects_dropped_on_New_Year%27s_Eve" title="List of objects dropped on New Year's Eve">similar events</a> outside of New York City, where a ball or other item is lowered or raised in an identical manner. The items used for these events often represent local culture or history: <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Peach_Drop" title="Peach Drop">Peach Drop</a> reflects <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>'s identity as the "Peach State".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mentalfloss-weirditems_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mentalfloss-weirditems-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New York City and Times Square serve as the focal point for national media coverage of the holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Bandleader <a href="/wiki/Guy_Lombardo" title="Guy Lombardo">Guy Lombardo</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Big_band" title="Big band">band</a>—The Royal Canadians—were well known for their annual <a href="/wiki/Big_band_remote" title="Big band remote">broadcast</a> from New York City. Their signature performance of "<a href="/wiki/Auld_Lang_Syne" title="Auld Lang Syne">Auld Lang Syne</a>" at midnight helped make the <a href="/wiki/Traditional_pop_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditional pop music">standard</a> synonymous with the holiday. Beginning on <a href="/wiki/Big_band_remote" title="Big band remote">radio</a> in 1929, Lombardo moved to <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> television from 1956 to 1976, adding coverage of the ball drop.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ppg-Lombardo_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ppg-Lombardo-46">[46]</a></sup> Following Lombardo's death, <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark%27s_New_Year%27s_Rockin%27_Eve" title="Dick Clark's New Year's Rockin' Eve">New Year's Rockin' Eve</a></i> (which premiered for 1973 on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>, and moved to <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> for 1975) became the dominant New Year's Eve <a href="/wiki/Television_special" title="Television special">special</a> on U.S. television—especially among younger viewers—with Clark having anchored New Year's coverage (including <i>New Year's Rockin' Eve</i> and the one-off <i><a href="/wiki/ABC_2000_Today" title="ABC 2000 Today">ABC 2000 Today</a></i>) for 33 straight years. After Clark suffered a <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a> in December 2004, fellow television personality <a href="/wiki/Regis_Philbin" title="Regis Philbin">Regis Philbin</a> guest hosted the 2005 edition. Due to a lingering <a href="/wiki/Speech_impediment" class="mw-redirect" title="Speech impediment">speech impediment</a> brought upon by the stroke, Clark retired as host and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a> for 2006, but continued making limited appearances on the special until his death in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-dc72-usatoday_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dc72-usatoday-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-abcnews1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcnews1-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-latimes_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2012Edition_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012Edition-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thr-nyre2013details_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr-nyre2013details-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other notable celebrations include the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/America%27s_Party" title="America's Party">America's Party</a>", which consists of a ticketed concert event at the <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Street_Experience" title="Fremont Street Experience">Fremont Street Experience</a>, and a public fireworks show at midnight that is launched from multiple casinos on the Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-fourcities_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-fourcities-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, a city long without a major public New Year celebration, held an inaugural gathering in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">Downtown</a>'s newly completed <a href="/wiki/Grand_Park" title="Grand Park">Grand Park</a> to celebrate the beginning of 2014. The event included food trucks, art installations, and culminating with a <a href="/wiki/Projection_mapping" title="Projection mapping">projection mapping</a> show on the side of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_Hall" title="Los Angeles City Hall">Los Angeles City Hall</a> near midnight. The inaugural event drew over 25,000 spectators and participants.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> For 2016, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> introduced an event known as Chi-Town Rising.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Alongside the festivities in Times Square, New York's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> hosts a "Midnight Run" event organized by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Road_Runners" title="New York Road Runners">New York Road Runners</a>, which features a fireworks show and a footrace around the park that begins at the stroke of midnight.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-fourcities_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-fourcities-54">[54]</a></sup> Since 2014–15, musician <a href="/wiki/Pitbull_(rapper)" title="Pitbull (rapper)">Pitbull</a> has hosted a New Year's Eve concert at <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bayfront_Park" title="Bayfront Park">Bayfront Park</a> (which was initially televised as a New Year's special on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pitbull%27s_New_Year%27s_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitbull's New Year's Revolution">Pitbull's New Year's Revolution</a></i>, until 2017–18).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Major <a href="/wiki/Theme_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme park">theme parks</a> also hold New Year's celebrations; <a href="/wiki/Disney_theme_parks" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney theme parks">Disney theme parks</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Resort" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney World Resort">Walt Disney World Resort</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disneyland" title="Disneyland">Disneyland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>, are traditionally the busiest around the Christmas and New Year's holidays.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-fourcities_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-fourcities-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wesh-busiest_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wesh-busiest-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_observances">Religious observances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religious observances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, 1 January is a <a href="/wiki/Solemnity" title="Solemnity">solemnity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Circumcision_of_Christ" title="Feast of the Circumcision of Christ">Feast of the Circumcision of Christ</a>, honoring the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary">Blessed Virgin Mary</a>, the Mother of Jesus; it is a <a href="/wiki/Holy_Day_of_Obligation" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Day of Obligation">Holy Day of Obligation</a> in most countries (<a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> being a notable exception), thus the Church requires the attendance of all Catholics in such countries for <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> that day. However a vigil Mass may be held on the evening before a Holy Day; thus it has become customary to celebrate Mass on the evening of New Year's Eve. (New Year's Eve is a <a href="/wiki/Silvester" class="mw-redirect" title="Silvester">feast day</a> honoring <a href="/wiki/Pope_Sylvester_I" title="Pope Sylvester I">Pope Sylvester I</a> in the Roman Catholic calendar, but it is not widely recognized in the United States.)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Many Christian congregations have New Year's Eve <a href="/wiki/Watchnight_service" title="Watchnight service">watchnight services</a>. Some, especially <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodists</a> and those in the <a href="/wiki/Black_church" title="Black church">African American community</a>, have a tradition known as "Watch Night", in which the faithful congregate in services continuing past midnight, giving thanks for the blessings of the outgoing year and praying for divine favor during the upcoming year. In the English-speaking world, Watch Night can be traced back to <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a>, the founder of Methodism,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> who learned the custom from the <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Brethren" class="mw-redirect" title="Moravian Brethren">Moravian Brethren</a> who came to England in the 1730s. Moravian congregations still observe the Watch Night service on New Year's Eve. Watch Night took on special significance to African Americans on New Year's Eve 1862, as slaves anticipated the arrival of 1 January 1863, when <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Lincoln</a> had announced he would sign the <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation Proclamation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Radio specials give a countdown and announce the New Year. In <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, the bells of the Cathedral of Caracas ring twelve times.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> During these special programs, is a tradition to broadcast songs about the end of the year. It is a non-working holiday. Popular songs include "Viejo año" ("Old year"), by <a href="/wiki/Gaita_Zuliana" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaita Zuliana">Gaita</a> group <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo_15" title="Maracaibo 15">Maracaibo 15</a>, and "Cinco pa' las 12" ("Five minutes before twelve"), which was versioned by several popular singers including Nestor Zavarce, Nancy Ramos and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_El_Puma" class="mw-redirect" title="José Luis Rodríguez El Puma">José Luis Rodríguez El Puma</a>. The unofficial hymn for the first minutes of the New Year is "Año Nuevo, Vida Nueva" ("New Year, New Life"), by the band Billo's Caracas Boys. Many people play the national anthem in their houses. </p>
      <p>Traditions include wearing yellow underwear, eating <a href="/wiki/Pan_de_jam%C3%B3n" title="Pan de jamón">Pan de jamón</a>, and 12 grapes with sparkling wine. </p>
      <p>Special holiday programs are broadcast on Venezuelan television stations including <a href="/wiki/Venevision" class="mw-redirect" title="Venevision">Venevision</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The New Year celebrations take place in all around the country mostly in <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sylhet" title="Sylhet">Sylhet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajshahi" title="Rajshahi">Rajshahi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khulna" title="Khulna">Khulna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barishal" class="mw-redirect" title="Barishal">Barishal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar" title="Cox's Bazar">Cox's Bazar</a> etc. The celebrations mostly take place at night. On this day, people go to the parties at club or hotels, beaches, at the crowdy roadsides and bridges where firecrackers are blast out in the sky at night. The roadsides and bridges are also lighted up by colourful lights at night. People do a get-together as well as enjoy with their families. That day, <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar" title="Cox's Bazar">Cox's Bazar</a> becomes a popular tourist destination for both <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a> and foreign tourists. </p>
      <p>Music, songs and dances are organized in the auditoriums, hotels, beaches and as well as in the grounds which are shown live concert on <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">T.V</a> where many <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bangladesh" title="Cinema of Bangladesh">Dhallywood</a> celebrities along with many personalities participate in the dance, music, songs and often drama to liven up the concert more. Sometimes marriages and weddings take place in the clubs at night of 31 December so that the people can enjoy more.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> People also enjoy the New Year's Eve with their families, relatives and friends in the ships and yachts specially in the sea while going to <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Island" title="St. Martin's Island">Saint Martin</a> where DJs liven up their night through their music and songs.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> during the year's last <a href="/wiki/Jumu%27ah" title="Jumu'ah">Jumma</a> prayer of mosque permanently pray a Munajat (which is done all over the mosques of the country) so that <a href="/wiki/Allah" title="Allah">Allah</a> may bless them and the coming year can be fruitful.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> organize a Puja so that the coming year can be fruitful for them. The <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> go to the churches for a watch night service till midnight, praying for blessing in the coming new year as it is also part of the <a href="/wiki/Christmastide" title="Christmastide">Christmastide</a> season observances. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, although the celebrations of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Lunar New Year</a> are not until a few weeks after the Gregorian New Year, celebrations of the Gregorian New Year are held in some areas, particularly in major cities. For example, celebrations with fireworks and rock concerts have taken place in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>'s Solana Blue Harbor Shopping Park, while cultural shows and other events are held at the city's Millennium Monument, <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Green" title="Olympic Green">Olympic Green</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Palace" title="Summer Palace">Summer Palace</a>. Since 2011, a light and sound show has been held at <a href="/wiki/The_Bund_(Shanghai)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bund (Shanghai)">The Bund</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, a few minutes before midnight.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HK_NYE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HK_NYE.jpg/220px-HK_NYE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HK_NYE.jpg/330px-HK_NYE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HK_NYE.jpg/440px-HK_NYE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3266" data-file-height="2178"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HK_NYE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fireworks display in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, many gather in shopping districts like <a href="/wiki/Central,_Hong_Kong" title="Central, Hong Kong">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Causeway_Bay" title="Causeway Bay">Causeway Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsim_Sha_Tsui" title="Tsim Sha Tsui">Tsim Sha Tsui</a>. Beginning in 2008, a 60-second numerical countdown to New Year's, consisting of <a href="/wiki/LED" class="mw-redirect" title="LED">LED</a> lights and pyrotechnic display effects, on the facade of <a href="/wiki/Two_International_Finance_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Two International Finance Centre">Two International Finance Centre</a> was launched, followed by a fireworks display, alongside an exhibition of the <a href="/wiki/A_Symphony_of_Lights" title="A Symphony of Lights">Symphony of Lights</a>. For the arrival of 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Convention_and_Exhibition_Centre" title="Hong Kong Convention and Exhibition Centre">Hong Kong Convention and Exhibition Centre</a> initiated the countdown, while the fireworks display and A Symphony of Lights show were extended to eight minutes. </p>
      <p>Shopping malls are often major celebration venues. The <a href="/wiki/Times_Square_(Hong_Kong)" title="Times Square (Hong Kong)">Times Square</a> shopping mall, for instance, holds their own celebration of the ball drop held at <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. There are also various district-wide celebrations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Asia">Central Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Central Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, New Year's Eve celebrations were inherited from Soviet traditions; thus they are similar to those of Russia. An example of such traditions would be the playing of the national anthem at midnight and the presidential address before it. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In India as a land of diverse cultures and practices, apart from the Gregorian new year, there are Parsi New Year, Hindu New Year (which might differ from region to region), Muslim New Year, etc. Celebration for culture-specific new years is different from the celebrations of the Gregorian new year. Gregorian new year celebration is mostly by way of parties late night and a working holiday followed by it. Most celebrations for 31 December take place in the major metropolitan cities like <a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chandigarh" title="Chandigarh">Chandigarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>. New Year is also celebrated in other cities and towns around the country like <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhubaneswar" title="Bhubaneswar">Bhubaneswar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore" title="Coimbatore">Coimbatore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuttack" title="Cuttack">Cuttack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vadodara" title="Vadodara">Vadodara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vijayawada" title="Vijayawada">Vijayawada</a>. There are many shows, events, awards and parties organized all over India. Big and small celebrities and personalities perform as well as enjoy in these parties. Many discos and pubs organize big singers, DJs or local talent to liven up the night with their music and songs. <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a> are the most visited destinations during New Year celebrations both by Indian and foreign tourists. </p>
      <p>Major events like live concerts and dances by film and music stars are also organized and attended mostly by youngsters. More often people like to celebrate New Year Eve with their family. Hotels and resorts are also decked up in anticipation of tourist arrival and intense competition makes them entice the tourists with exciting New Year offers. Many people across the country also follow old traditions. The <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> community often go to church for a watch night service till midnight praying for blessing in the coming new year. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cmisoka" title="Ōmisoka">Ōmisoka</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg/180px-Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg/270px-Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg/360px-Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3058" data-file-height="5337"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_Tower_in_New_Year%27s_Eve_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tokyo Tower on New Year's Eve, 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, New Year's Eve is used to prepare for and welcome <i>Toshigami</i> (年神), the New Year's god. People clean their homes and prepare <a href="/wiki/Kadomatsu" title="Kadomatsu">Kadomatsu</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shimenawa" title="Shimenawa">Shimenawa</a> to welcome the god before New Year's Eve. Buddhist temples ring their bells 108 times<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-68">[68]</a></sup> at midnight in the traditional <i>Joya no Kane</i> (除夜の鐘). The rings represent the 108 elements of <i><a href="/wiki/Kleshas_(Buddhism)" title="Kleshas (Buddhism)">bonō</a></i> (煩悩), mental states that lead people to take unwholesome actions. </p>
      <p>In most cities and urban areas across Japan, New Year's Eve celebrations are usually accompanied by concerts, countdowns, fireworks and other events. In <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, the two most crowded celebrations are held at the Shibuya crossing in <a href="/wiki/Shibuya,_Tokyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Shibuya, Tokyo">Shibuya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Z%C5%8Dj%C5%8D-ji" title="Zōjō-ji">Zojoji Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minato,_Tokyo" title="Minato, Tokyo">Minato</a>. People gather around the Zojoji Temple to release helium balloons with New Year's wishes up in the sky and watch the lighting of <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Tower" title="Tokyo Tower">Tokyo Tower</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Skytree" title="Tokyo Skytree">Tokyo Skytree</a> with a year number displayed on the observatory at the stroke of midnight. </p>
      <p>Three notable music-oriented television specials air near New Year's Eve. Since 1951, <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">NHK</a> has traditionally broadcast <i><a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dhaku_Uta_Gassen" title="Kōhaku Uta Gassen">Kōhaku Uta Gassen</a><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">紅白歌合戦</span>)</span></i> (<i>Red/White Singing Battle</i>) on New Year's Eve, a music competition where two teams of popular musicians (the red and white teams, which predominantly contain female and male performers respectively) perform songs, with the winning team determined by a panel of judges, audience members at the <a href="/wiki/NHK_Hall" title="NHK Hall">NHK Hall</a>, and televotes. The special is traditionally one of the most-watched television programs of the year in Japan. Although it did air on 31 December from 1959 to 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Record_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan Record Award">Japan Record Awards</a> ceremony, recognizing outstanding achievements in the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Japan" title="Music of Japan">Japanese music industry</a>, is held annually on 30 December since 2007 and is broadcast by <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">TBS</a>. Since 1996, <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuji Television">Fuji Television</a> has broadcast <i>Johnny's Countdown</i>—a live concert at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a> organized by the talent agency <a href="/wiki/Johnny_%26_Associates" title="Johnny &amp; Associates">Johnny &amp; Associates</a>. A newer tradition on New Year's Eve is <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">mixed martial arts</a>: promotions such as <a href="/wiki/Pride_Fighting_Championships" title="Pride Fighting Championships">Pride Fighting Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dream_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Dream (mixed martial arts)">DREAM</a>, <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> and now <a href="/wiki/Rizin_Fighting_Federation" title="Rizin Fighting Federation">Rizin</a> have hosted a large event each New Year's Eve at <a href="/wiki/Saitama_Super_Arena" title="Saitama Super Arena">Saitama Super Arena</a> since 2001. This card features highly-anticipated or title fights, and even special attractions such as Rizin's 2018 NYE card, which had as its main event an exhibition between kickboxing star <a href="/wiki/Tenshin_Nasukawa" title="Tenshin Nasukawa">Tenshin Nasukawa</a> and American boxing champion <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Mayweather_Jr." title="Floyd Mayweather Jr.">Floyd Mayweather Jr.</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korea">Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are two New Years celebrated in both <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, which are Lunar New Year and Solar New Year. The Solar New Year are always celebrated on the first day of January while Lunar New Year varies. Sometimes there are some traits that both North and South Korea celebrate, while some traits are celebrated differently or only on one side. </p>
      <p>In both Koreas, they call New Year's Day 설날 (Seollal). They eat a special soup called 떡국 (Tteokguk) which is a hot soup with thin, flat rice cakes and most of the times, eggs are inserted. The Koreans believe that one would get to earn one age if the soup is eaten New Year's Day. They say if one dares to not eat the soup on New Year's Day, then he or she will lose luck. </p>
      <p>Most cities and urban areas in both Koreas host New Year's Eve gatherings. In South Korea, two of the biggest celebrations take place in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>: the ringing of <a href="/wiki/Bosingak" title="Bosingak">Bosingak</a> bell 33 times at midnight and fireworks display at <a href="/wiki/Myeong-dong" title="Myeong-dong">Myeong-dong</a>, and an LED laser light show and fireworks display at the <a href="/wiki/Lotte_World_Tower" title="Lotte World Tower">Lotte World Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Songpa_District" title="Songpa District">Songpa-gu</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a>, North Korea, the chimes of the clock at the Grand People's Study House and the national fireworks display along <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung_Square" title="Kim Il-sung Square">Kim Il-sung Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juche_Tower" title="Juche Tower">Juche Tower</a> and the surrounding areas signal the start of the New Year. The celebration in Pyongyang, however, also marks the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/North_Korean_calendar" title="North Korean calendar">North Korean calendar</a> or the Juche Year, which is based on 15 April 1912, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a>'s date of birth, the celebrations are more recent in origin with the fireworks displays dating from 2013. </p>
      <p>For 2018-19, Kim Il-sung Square held its first large-scale public celebration, which featured a concert performance by the state <a href="/wiki/Moranbong_Band" title="Moranbong Band">Moranbong Band</a>, midnight fireworks, and a <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drone</a> light show.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On television, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a> held its annual drama awards show (<a href="/wiki/KBS_Drama_Awards" title="KBS Drama Awards">KBS Drama Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/SBS_Drama_Awards" title="SBS Drama Awards">SBS Drama Awards</a>) to honor the best drama programs throughout the year. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town,_Penang.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg/220px-2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg/330px-2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg/440px-2018_New_Year_Fireworks_in_George_Town%2C_Penang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1066" data-file-height="649"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
