         </div>Fireworks in <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Penang" title="George Town, Penang">George Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penang" title="Penang">Penang</a> on 1 January 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_(5309956791).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg/200px-MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg/300px-MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg/400px-MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_%285309956791%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2253" data-file-height="1222"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MALAM_TAHUN_BARU_(5309956791).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fireworks in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><i>Ambang Tahun Baru</i>, a celebration sponsored by the government was held at <a href="/wiki/Dataran_Merdeka" class="mw-redirect" title="Dataran Merdeka">Merdeka Square</a>, the field opposite the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building" title="Sultan Abdul Samad Building">Sultan Abdul Samad Building</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> capital of <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a> in the early days. The event was broadcast live on government as well as private TV stations at those times. Countdown is now broadcast live on Government televisions from <a href="/wiki/Putrajaya" title="Putrajaya">Putrajaya</a> and the Broadcasting centre which the concert is held and Fireworks are displayed at the <a href="/wiki/Petronas_Towers" title="Petronas Towers">Petronas Towers</a>. </p>
      <p>There are New Year countdown parties in major cities such as <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Penang" title="George Town, Penang">George Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shah_Alam" title="Shah Alam">Shah Alam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>, typically organised by the private sector in these cities.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongolia">Mongolia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mongolia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Mongolians began celebrating the Gregorian New Year in the Socialist period, with influence from the former Soviet Union. As a modern tradition, New Year's Eve as well as New Year's Day are public holidays, and are two of the biggest holidays of the year. They celebrate New Year's Eve with their family. It is common, just like in the former Soviet Union, that the <a href="/wiki/National_Anthem_of_Mongolia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Anthem of Mongolia">National Anthem of Mongolia</a> is to be played at the midnight hour on television. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve is usually celebrated with fireworks in big cities (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a>). Musical nights and concerts are also held.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Many Pakistani youngsters enjoy the type of celebrations held the world over. The elite and educated classes participate in night-long activities in urban and cosmopolitan cities like Karachi, Lahore, and the capital of Islamabad.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, New Year's Eve (<i>Bisperas ng Bagong Taon</i>) is a special non-working holiday. <a href="/wiki/Filipino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino people">Filipinos</a> usually celebrate New Year's Eve in the company of family or close friends. Traditionally, most households would visit the churches and attend year-end service and afterwards, would host or attend a midnight feast called the <i>Media Noche</i>. Typical dishes included holiday fare, <i><a href="/wiki/Pancit" title="Pancit">pancit</a></i> (for long life) and <i><a href="/wiki/Jam%C3%B3n" title="Jamón">Hamón</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Lechon" title="Lechon">Lechon</a></i> (roasted pig), is usually prepared, as is barbecued food. Some refrain from serving chicken, as their scratching and pecking for food is unlucky, being an idiom for a hand-to-mouth existence. </p>
      <p>Many opt to wear new, bright, or colourful clothes with circular patterns, such as <a href="/wiki/Polka_dot" title="Polka dot">polka dots</a>, or display sweets and twelve round fruits as the centrepiece, in the belief that circles attract money and fortune and that candies represent a sweeter year ahead. Several customs must only be done at midnight: some throw about coins to increase wealth in the coming year, or jump to increase their height, while some follow the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_influence_on_Filipino_culture" title="Spanish influence on Filipino culture">Spanish custom</a> of eating twelve grapes, one for each month of the year. People also make loud noises by blowing on cardboard or plastic horns, called <i>torotot</i>, banging on pots and pans, playing loud music, blowing car horns, or by igniting firecrackers, in the belief that the din scares away bad luck and evil spirits. <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_cannon" title="Bamboo cannon">Bamboo cannons</a> are also fired on the night in some places. </p>
      <p>Urban areas usually host many New Year's Eve parties and countdown celebrations hosted by the private sector with the help of the local government. These parties, which include balls hosted by hotels, usually display their own fireworks and are often very well-attended. Within Metro Manila, popular locations for celebrations include the area along <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a> at <a href="/wiki/Roxas_Boulevard" title="Roxas Boulevard">Roxas Boulevard</a> or <a href="/wiki/Luneta_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Luneta Park">Luneta Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, the intersection of Ayala and Makati Avenues in <a href="/wiki/Makati" title="Makati">Makati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resorts_World_Manila" title="Resorts World Manila">Resorts World Manila</a> and <a href="/wiki/SM_Mall_of_Asia" title="SM Mall of Asia">SM Mall of Asia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasay" title="Pasay">Pasay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quezon_Memorial_Circle" title="Quezon Memorial Circle">Quezon Memorial Circle</a> in Diliman and <a href="/wiki/Eastwood_City" title="Eastwood City">Eastwood City</a> in Libis, <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonifacio_Global_City" title="Bonifacio Global City">Bonifacio Global City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Taguig_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Taguig City">Taguig City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_City" title="Entertainment City">Entertainment City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Para%C3%B1aque" title="Parañaque">Parañaque City</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Arena" title="Philippine Arena">Philippine Arena</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_de_Victoria" title="Ciudad de Victoria">Ciudad de Victoria</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bocaue,_Bulacan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bocaue, Bulacan">Bocaue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria,_Bulacan" title="Santa Maria, Bulacan">Santa Maria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulacan" title="Bulacan">Bulacan</a>. Fireworks displays are also held in select cities in the regions. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg/220px-DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg/330px-DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg/440px-DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DSC_4864_2012_New_Year_Fireworks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A midnight fireworks show in <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay,_Singapore" title="Marina Bay, Singapore">Marina Bay, Singapore</a>, welcoming 2012.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New Year's celebrations in the city-state of <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> are centered upon <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay,_Singapore" title="Marina Bay, Singapore">Marina Bay</a>, which hosts a midnight fireworks show organized by the <a href="/wiki/Urban_Redevelopment_Authority" title="Urban Redevelopment Authority">Urban Redevelopment Authority</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Float_@_Marina_Bay" title="The Float @ Marina Bay">The Float @ Marina Bay</a> serves as the focal point of the event, with its ticketed grandstands and nearby buildings (such as hotels) being the most sought-after viewing locations for the show.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-72">[72]</a></sup> For the 2018–19 and 2019–20 editions, the fireworks were produced by Star Island—an <a href="/wiki/Avex_Group" title="Avex Group">Avex Group</a>-owned production that combines the fireworks with a large light show and other elements. For the 2019–20 edition, the production included a synchronized <a href="/wiki/Drone_display" title="Drone display">drone display</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-74">[74]</a></sup> Broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Mediacorp" title="Mediacorp">Mediacorp</a> organises a televised concert at The Promontory.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-74">[74]</a></sup> Smaller, local celebrations are also held outside of the downtown core.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg/200px-2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg/300px-2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg/400px-2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2009_Taipei_101_Love_Taiwan_Firework_from_upper_angle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Taipei 101 fireworks show in 2009.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most prominent New Year's event in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> is a major fireworks show launched from the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a> skyscraper in <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>. In 2018, the show was enhanced by the installation of a new LED display system on the north face of the tower between its 35th and 90th floors, which can be used to display digital animation effects. This change countered a reduction in the number of firework shells launched during the show, as part of an effort to produce less pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg/200px-Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg/300px-Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg/400px-Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_in_Bangkok_Thailand_2019_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fireworks at Chao Phraya River in Bangkok, Thailand 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Aside from the traditional Thai New Year called <i><a href="/wiki/Songkran_(Thailand)" title="Songkran (Thailand)">Songkran (Thailand)</a></i> (which falls on 13 April or 14 April), Thais also celebrate the arrival of the Gregorian New Year on 1 January with their families, relatives and friends, which includes a family dinner and following different customs. It is a public holiday. In most cities and urban areas across <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, New Year's Eve celebrations are accompanied by countdowns, fireworks, concerts and other major events, notably, the CentralWorld Square at <a href="/wiki/CentralWorld" title="CentralWorld">CentralWorld</a> and the area along <a href="/wiki/Chao_Phraya_River" title="Chao Phraya River">Chao Phraya River</a> at <a href="/wiki/ICONSIAM" class="mw-redirect" title="ICONSIAM">ICONSIAM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asiatique" title="Asiatique">Asiatique</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, and the Pattaya Beach in <a href="/wiki/Pattaya" title="Pattaya">Pattaya</a>, while public places such as hotels, pubs, restaurants and nightclubs, also host New Year's Eve parties by offering food, entertainment and music to the guests, and they usually stay open until the next morning. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albania">Albania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Albania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Preparations for New Year's Eve in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> start with the Christmas tree, which in Albania is known as "New Year's Tree" or "New Year's Pine". At midnight, everyone toasts and greets each other and fireworks are lit. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, New Year's Eve is usually celebrated with friends and family. At exactly midnight, all radio and television programmes operated by <a href="/wiki/ORF_(broadcaster)" title="ORF (broadcaster)">ORF</a> broadcast the sound of the <a href="/wiki/Pummerin" title="Pummerin">Pummerin</a>, the bell of <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, followed by the <i>Donauwalzer</i> ("<a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Danube" title="The Blue Danube">The Blue Danube</a>") by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_II" title="Johann Strauss II">Johann Strauss II</a>. Many people dance to this at parties or in the street. Large crowds gather in the streets of Vienna, where the municipal government organises a series of stages where bands and orchestras play. Fireworks are set off by both municipal governments and individuals. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, New Year's Eve (<i>Sint Sylvester Vooravond</i> ("Saint Sylvester's Eve") or <i>Oudjaar</i> ("old year")) is celebrated with family parties, called <i>réveillons</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">French speaking areas</a>. On television, a stand-up comedian reviews the past year after which a musical or variety show signals midnight, when everyone kisses, exchanges good luck greetings, and toasts the New Year and absent relatives and friends with <a href="/wiki/Champagne_(wine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Champagne (wine)">champagne</a>. Many people light fireworks or go into the street to watch them. Most cities have their own fireworks display: the most famous is at <a href="/wiki/Mont_des_Arts" title="Mont des Arts">Mont des Arts</a> in Brussels. Cities, cafés and restaurants are crowded. Free bus services and special New Year's Eve taxis (the <i>Responsible Young Drivers</i>) bring everyone home afterwards. </p>
      <p>On 1 January (<i>Nieuwjaarsdag</i> in Dutch) children read their "New Year's letter" and give holiday greeting cards of decorated paper featuring golden cherubs and angels, colored roses and ribbon-tied garlands to parents and godparents, on decorated paper. </p>
      <p>Belgian farmers also wish their animals a happy New Year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year is widely celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a>. Streets are decorated for New Year's Eve and there is a fireworks show and concerts in all the larger cities. Restaurants, clubs, cafes and hotels are usually full of guests and they organize New Year's Eve parties. </p>
      <p>In Sarajevo, people gather in the Square of children of Sarajevo where a local rock band entertains them. Several trumpet and rock groups play until the early morning hours. At midnight there is a big fireworks show. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Czech_Republic.2FSlovakia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic/Slovakia">Czech Republic/Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Czech Republic/Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year!_(23741249829).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg/250px-Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg/375px-Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg/500px-Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year%21_%2823741249829%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2490" data-file-height="1660"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prague_New_Year_2016_fireworks._Happy_New_Year!_(23741249829).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> New Year Fireworks
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New Year's Eve (<i>Silvestr/Silvester</i>) celebrations and traditions in <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> are very similar. New Year's Eve is the noisiest day of the year. People generally gather with friends at parties, in pubs, clubs, in the streets, or city squares to eat, drink, and celebrate the new year. Fireworks are a popular tradition; in large cities such as <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, the fireworks start before noon and steadily increase until midnight. In the first minutes after midnight, people toast with champagne, wish each other a happy new year, fortune and health, and go outside for the fireworks. </p>
      <p>In both countries all major TV stations air entertainment shows before and after the midnight countdown, which is followed by the National anthem of each country. The Presidents of the republics gave their New Year speech in the morning – the new Czech President Miloš Zeman renewed the tradition of Christmas speeches. In recent years however the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovak</a> national anthem is played at midnight, in honor of the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">shared history of both nations</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CopenhagenNYE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/CopenhagenNYE.jpg/250px-CopenhagenNYE.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/CopenhagenNYE.jpg/375px-CopenhagenNYE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/CopenhagenNYE.jpg/500px-CopenhagenNYE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CopenhagenNYE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>New Year fireworks over <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>People in <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> may go to parties or entertain guests at home. There is a special evening meal that concludes with <a href="/wiki/Kransekage" class="mw-redirect" title="Kransekage">Kransekage</a>, a special dessert, along with champagne. Other traditional dishes are boiled cod, stewed kale and cured saddle of pork.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> However, expensive cuts of beef as well as sushi have become increasingly popular.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Multiple significant traditional events are broadcast on television and radio on 31 December. This includes, but is not limited to: </p>
      <p>The monarch's New Year message from <a href="/wiki/Amalienborg_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Amalienborg Palace">Amalienborg Palace</a><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> at 18:00 and the Town Hall Clock in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> striking midnight. Thousands of people gather together in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A5dhuspladsen" class="mw-redirect" title="Rådhuspladsen">Rådhuspladsen</a> (the Town Hall Square) and cheer.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Life_Guards_(Denmark)" title="Royal Life Guards (Denmark)">Royal Guard</a><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> parade in their red gala uniforms. The climax of the celebration is fireworks launched as the Town Hall Tower bells chime on the stroke of midnight. After midnight, all radio &amp; television stations play: "<a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A6r_velkommen,_Herrens_%C3%A5r&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vær velkommen, Herrens år (page does not exist)">Vær velkommen, Herrens år</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://da.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C3%A6r_velkommen,_Herrens_%C3%A5r" class="extiw" title="da:Vær velkommen, Herrens år">da</a>]</span>" [Danish new year's hymn] and followed by "<a href="/wiki/Kong_Christian_stod_ved_h%C3%B8jen_mast" title="Kong Christian stod ved højen mast">Kong Christian stod ved højen mast</a>" [Danish Royal Anthem] and "<a href="/wiki/Der_er_et_yndigt_land" title="Der er et yndigt land">Der er et yndigt land</a>" [Danish National Anthem].<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like in the surrounding nations, the German comedy sketch <i><a href="/wiki/Dinner_for_One" title="Dinner for One">Dinner for One</a></i> is broadcast every year at 23:45, and ends just minutes before the new year. This has been a tradition every year since 1980 (except in 1985). </p>
      <p>Another reoccurring broadcast is the 1968 film <a href="/wiki/The_Party_(1968_film)" title="The Party (1968 film)"><i>The Party</i></a>, which is aired after midnight on 1 January. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Estonia">Estonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Estonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>To celebrate New Year's Eve in <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, people decorate villages, visit friends and prepare lavish meals. </p>
      <p>Some believe that people should eat seven, nine, or twelve times on New Year's Eve. These are lucky numbers in Estonia; it is believed that for each meal consumed, the person gains the strength of that many men the following year. Meals should not be completely finished—some food should be left for ancestors and spirits who visit the house on New Year's Eve. </p>
      <p>Traditional New Year food includes pork with sauerkraut or Estonian sauerkraut (<i>mulgikapsad</i>), baked potatoes and swedes with hog's head, and white and blood sausage. Vegetarians can eat potato salad with navy beet<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and pâté. Gingerbread and marzipan are very popular for dessert. Traditional New Year drinks include beer and mead, but mulled wine and champagne have become modern favourites. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, New Year's Eve is usually celebrated with family or friends. Late supper is served, often featuring wieners, <a href="/wiki/Janssons_frestelse" class="mw-redirect" title="Janssons frestelse">Janssons frestelse</a>, and potato salad. Some municipalities organize fireworks at midnight. Consumer fireworks are also very popular. A Finnish tradition is <a href="/wiki/Molybdomancy" title="Molybdomancy">molybdomancy</a> – to tell the fortunes of the New Year by melting "tin" (actually lead) in a tiny pan on the stove and throwing it quickly in a bucket of cold water. The resulting blob of metal is analyzed, for example by interpreting shadows it casts by candlelight. These predictions are however never taken seriously. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/YLE" class="mw-redirect" title="YLE">YLE</a> broadcasts the reception of the New Year at <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Senate_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Helsinki Senate Square">Helsinki Senate Square</a>. Countdown to New Year is with the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Cathedral" title="Helsinki Cathedral">Helsinki Cathedral</a> clock. In the afternoon programme, the German comedy sketch <i><a href="/wiki/Dinner_for_One" title="Dinner for One">Dinner for One</a></i> is shown every year. On the radio, just before midnight, the poem <i>Hymyilevä Apollo</i> (Smiling Apollo) by <a href="/wiki/Eino_Leino" title="Eino Leino">Eino Leino</a> is read.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

         <img alt="File:Eiffel Tower on the New Year Eve at midnight.webm" style="width:220px;height:124px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Eiffel_Tower_on_the_New_Year_Eve_at_midnight.webm/220px--Eiffel_Tower_on_the_New_Year_Eve_at_midnight.webm.jpg"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/Eiffel_Tower_on_the_New_Year_Eve_at_midnight.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eiffel_Tower_on_the_New_Year_Eve_at_midnight.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>(video) Celebrations in 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, New Year's Eve (<i>la Saint-Sylvestre</i>) is usually celebrated with a feast, <i>le Réveillon de la Saint-Sylvestre</i><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> (<i>Cap d'Any</i> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalonia" title="Northern Catalonia">Northern Catalonia</a>). This feast customarily includes special dishes including <a href="/wiki/Foie_gras" title="Foie gras">foie gras</a>, seafood such as oysters, and <a href="/wiki/Champagne_(wine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Champagne (wine)">champagne</a>. The celebration can be a simple, intimate dinner with friends and family or, <i>une soirée dansante</i>, a much fancier ball. </p>
      <p>On New Year's Day (<i>le Jour de l'An</i>) friends and family exchange <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_resolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="New Year's resolutions">New Year's resolutions</a>, kisses, and wishes. Some people eat <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, parties are common on New Year's Eve. Fireworks are very popular, both with individuals and at large municipal displays. 31 December and the three days leading up to it are the only four days of the year on which fireworks may be sold in Germany. Every year <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> hosts one of the largest New Year's Eve celebrations in all of Europe, attended by over a million people. The focal point is the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, where midnight fireworks are centered, with a live broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Zweites_Deutsches_Fernsehen" class="mw-redirect" title="Zweites Deutsches Fernsehen">2DF</a> under the name <i>Willkommen</i> with musical guests. Germans toast the New Year with a glass of <a href="/wiki/Sparkling_wine#Sekt" title="Sparkling wine">Sekt</a> (German sparkling wine) or champagne.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Molybdomancy" title="Molybdomancy">Molybdomancy</a> <i lang="de" title="German-language text">(Bleigießen)</i> is another German New Year's Eve tradition, which involves telling fortunes by the shapes made by molten lead dropped into cold water. Other auspicious actions are to touch a chimney sweep or rub some ash on your forehead for good luck and health. <a href="/wiki/Berliner_(doughnut)" title="Berliner (doughnut)">Jam-filled doughnuts</a> with or without alcoholic fillings are eaten. Finally a tiny <a href="/wiki/Marzipan_pig" title="Marzipan pig">marzipan pig</a> is consumed for more good luck.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In some northern regions of Germany (e.g. <a href="/wiki/East_Frisia" title="East Frisia">East Frisia</a>) the making of <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Speckendicken&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Speckendicken (page does not exist)">Speckendicken</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speckendicken" class="extiw" title="de:Speckendicken">de</a>]</span></i> (also <i lang="de" title="German-language text">Speckdicken</i>) is another tradition – people go door to door visiting their neighbors and partaking in this dish. It looks similar to a pancake, but the recipe calls for either dark molasses or dark syrup, topped with a few <a href="/wiki/Mettwurst" title="Mettwurst">mettwurst</a> slices and bacon strips.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another notable tradition is the British comedy sketch <i><a href="/wiki/Dinner_for_One" title="Dinner for One">Dinner for One</a></i>, which has traditionally been broadcast on German television on New Year's Eve since 1972. The version traditionally broadcast on German television was originally recorded in 1963, and was occasionally used as filler programming by <a href="/wiki/Norddeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Norddeutscher Rundfunk">NDR</a> due to popular demand; in 1972, <i>Dinner for One</i> received its traditional New Year's Eve scheduling. The sketch, as well as its catchphrase "the same procedure as every year", are well known in German pop culture. <i>Dinner for One</i> is also broadcast on or around New Year's Eve in other European countries, although it is, ironically, relatively unknown in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-slate-dinnerforone_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slate-dinnerforone-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A midnight fireworks display is held over the historic <a href="/wiki/Parthenon" title="Parthenon">Parthenon</a> temple in the capital of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A common tradition among <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox">Greek Orthodox</a> families is the cutting of a <a href="/wiki/Vasilopita" title="Vasilopita">vasilopita</a> ("King's pie" or "St. Basil's pie") at midnight. A coin or similar object is usually baked inside, and whoever finds it is said to have luck over the next year. New Year's Day is considered a feast day for <a href="/wiki/Basil_of_Caesarea" title="Basil of Caesarea">Basil of Caesarea</a>, and it is also considered a custom to reserve the first slice of the vasilopita for St. Basil.<sup id="cite_ref-Kochilas_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kochilas-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Szilveszter_2017.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Szilveszter_2017.png/220px-Szilveszter_2017.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Szilveszter_2017.png/330px-Szilveszter_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Szilveszter_2017.png/440px-Szilveszter_2017.png 2x" data-file-width="1681" data-file-height="931"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Szilveszter_2017.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Midnight – Millenáris, NYE 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New Year's Eve (<i>Szilveszter</i>) in Hungary is celebrated with home parties and street parties, including a gathering in downtown <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>. Fireworks and firecrackers are popular. Champagne, wine and traditional Hungarian New Year dishes—frankfurter sausages with <a href="/wiki/Horseradish" title="Horseradish">horseradish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lentil_soup" title="Lentil soup">lentil soup</a>, fish, and roast pig—are consumed. The national anthem is commonly sung at midnight. </p>
      <p>In past centuries, some Hungarians believed that animals were able to speak on New Year's Eve, and that onion skins sprinkled with salt could indicate a rainy month. </p>
      <p>Hungarian Christian communities focus on celebrating Mass on both New Year's Eve and New Year's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg/220px-NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg/330px-NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg/440px-NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="670"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NewYearFireworks-Reykjavik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>New Year fireworks over <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Fireworks are very popular in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, particularly on New Year's Eve. Iceland's biggest New Year's Eve events are usually in and around the capital, <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a>. </p>
      <p>Since the 1940s, state broadcaster <a href="/wiki/R%C3%9AV_(TV_channel)" title="RÚV (TV channel)">RÚV</a> has traditionally broadcast <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%81ram%C3%B3taskaupi%C3%B0" title="Áramótaskaupið">Áramótaskaupið</a></i> (literally <i>The New Year's Comedy</i>), a special which features <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">comedy sketches</a> satirizing the events and news headlines of the past year. Originating from radio and later moving to television, the special is the most-watched television program of the year in Iceland (with an estimated 75% of the population having watched the special in 2018, across 98% of all televisions in the country), and some of its sketches—such as a 1989 sketch that portrayed then <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Iceland)" title="Ministry of Finance (Iceland)">Minister of Finance</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%93lafur_Ragnar_Gr%C3%ADmsson" title="Ólafur Ragnar Grímsson">Ólafur Ragnar Grímsson</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a>-esque superhero known as "Skattmann" ("Taxman")—have become well known in local popular culture.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p> New Year's Eve (<i>Oíche Chinn Bliana</i>, <i>Oíche na Coda Móire</i>, or <i>Oíche Chaille,</i> the night of big portion)<sup id="cite_ref-:3_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-96">[96]</a></sup> when traditionally households would partake in a large feast that was believed to ensure a plentiful new year.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-97">[97]</a></sup> Beliefs around the day meant that no food or other goods would be taken from the house, to guard against less or hunger in the year to come, believing that if anything was taken from the house on this day the house would remain empty for the year and have no luck. It was traditional for no water to be drawn from a well after sunset.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Even the homeless and those in need would not be offered food or alms on this day. In many of the country, a large <a href="/wiki/Barmbrack" title="Barmbrack">barmbrack</a> would be baked during the day, with the man of the house taking three large bites of the cake in the evening, and throwing it against the inside of the front door as an offering to the <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Holy Trinity</a>. An invocation accompanied this:</p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>"Fógraímíd an gorta </p>
       <p>Amach to tír na dTurcach; </p>
       <p>Ó 'nocht go bliain ó 'nocht </p>
       <p> Agus 'nocht féin amach"<sup id="cite_ref-:4_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>This translates as "We warn famine to retire, To the land of the Turks; From tonight to this night twelve months, And from this night itself." The bits of cake would be gathered, and eaten by the family.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-97">[97]</a></sup> Other variations include throwing the cake to someone outside the door, or conducting the ritual in the stables or other animal housing.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-96">[96]</a></sup> Church bells ringing, the lighting of bonfires, and singing would take place towards midnight.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In modern times, celebrations in major cities are modest, with most people favouring small parties in the home for family and friends. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, New Year's Eve (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Vigilia di Capodanno</i> or <i>Notte di San Silvestro</i>) is celebrated by the observation of traditional rituals, such as wearing red <a href="/wiki/Underwear" class="mw-redirect" title="Underwear">underwear</a>. An ancient tradition in southern regions which is rarely followed today was disposing of old or unused items by dropping them from the window. </p>
      <p>Dinner is traditionally eaten with relatives and friends. It often includes <a href="/wiki/Zampone" class="mw-redirect" title="Zampone">zampone</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cotechino" title="Cotechino">cotechino</a> (a meal made with <a href="/wiki/Pig%27s_trotters" title="Pig's trotters">pig's trotters</a> or entrails), and lentils. At 20:30, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Italy" title="President of Italy">President of the Republic</a> reads a television message of greetings to Italians. </p>
      <p>At midnight, fireworks are displayed all across the country. Rarely followed today is the tradition that consist in eating <a href="/wiki/Lentil" title="Lentil">lentil</a> stew when the bell tolls midnight, one spoonful per bell. This is supposed to bring good fortune; the round lentils represent coins. </p>
      <p>On television, <a href="/wiki/Rai_1" title="Rai 1">Rai 1</a> broadcasts a special to welcome the New Year at 21:00 called <i>L'anno che verrà</i> with musical guests, surprises and many more. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> organized its first New Year's street party in 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Floriana" title="Floriana">Floriana</a>. The event was not highly advertised and proved controversial, due to the closing of an arterial street for the day. In 2010 there were the first national celebrations in <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George's Square">St. George's Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Although professional fireworks are very popular in Malta, they are almost totally absent on New Year's Eve. Usually the Maltese hit nightclubs and specific dance music parties to celebrate New Year's Eve. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montenegro">Montenegro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Montenegro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, New Year's Eve celebrations are held in all large cities, usually accompanied by fireworks. It is usually celebrated with family or friends, at home or outside. Restaurants, clubs, cafés and hotels organize celebrations with food and music. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve (<i>Oud en Nieuw</i> or <i>Oudejaarsavond</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> is usually celebrated as a cozy evening with family or friends, although many people attend big organized parties. Traditional snack foods are <i><a href="/wiki/Oliebol" title="Oliebol">oliebollen</a></i> (dutch doughnuts) and <i>appelbeignets</i> (apple slice <a href="/wiki/Fritter" title="Fritter">fritters</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> On television, the main feature is the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oudejaarsconference&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oudejaarsconference (page does not exist)">oudejaarsconference</a></i>, a performance by one of the major Dutch <a href="/wiki/Kleinkunst" class="mw-redirect" title="Kleinkunst">cabaretiers</a> (comparable to <a href="/wiki/Stand-up_comedy" title="Stand-up comedy">stand-up comedy</a>, but more serious, generally including a satirical review of the year's politics). Historically, in <a href="/wiki/Reformed_churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed churches">Reformed</a> Protestant families, <a href="/wiki/Psalm_90" title="Psalm 90">Psalm 90</a> is read, although this tradition is now fading away.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> At midnight, <a href="/wiki/Mulled_wine" title="Mulled wine">Glühwein</a> <i>(bishops wine)</i> or champagne is drunk. Many people light their own fireworks. Towns do not organize a central fireworks display, except for <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> where the national fireworks display can be seen near the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Erasmus Bridge">Erasmus Bridge</a>. In rural areas, the tradition of <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbidschieten" class="extiw" title="nl:Carbidschieten">nl:Carbidschieten</a> (<i>blasting off footballs or churnlids with <a href="/wiki/Calcium_carbide" title="Calcium carbide">Calcium carbide</a> gas filled milk churns</i>) is performed instead of lighting fireworks. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Macedonia">North Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: North Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve is celebrated across <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>. New Year's Day is celebrated by day-long fireworks shows. The day is celebrated together with family or friends at home or in restaurants, clubs, cafés and hotels. During the day-time celebration, children get gifts. Evening celebrations include food, music, and dancing to both traditional Macedonian folk music, and modern music. New Year's Eve is celebrated on 31 December and also on 14 January according to the Macedonian Orthodox Calendar. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> New Year's Eve (<i>Nyttårsaften</i>) is the second biggest celebration of the year, after <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">Christmas Eve</a>. While Christmas Eve is a family celebration, New Year's Eve is an opportunity to celebrate with friends.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditionally, there is first a feast, commonly consisting of stuffed, roast turkey with potatoes, sprouts, gravy and <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_salad" title="Waldorf salad">Waldorf salad</a>. The accompanying beverage is traditionally beer (commonly either Christmas beer or lager beer). Dessert will often be vanilla pudding or rice cream, and there will be cakes and coffee later in the evening – commonly accompanied by a glass of cognac. Then, at close to 12<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am on New Year's Day, people will go outside to send up fireworks. Fireworks are only permitted to be sold to the general public on the days leading up to New Year's Eve, and only to be launched that night. </p>
      <p>Due to the general use of fireworks, more fires occur on New Year's Eve than on any other day of the year in Norway. Accordingly, most Norwegian cities, and many towns, host a large, public fireworks display in order to discourage private use of fireworks in built-up areas. People will then congregate in a central square or similar to watch and celebrate. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> New Year's Eve (<i>Sylwester</i>) celebrations include both indoor and outdoor festivities. A large open-air concert is held in the <a href="/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Market Square, Kraków">Main Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>. 150,000 to 200,000 revelers celebrate the New Year with live music and a fireworks display over <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków">St. Mary's Basilica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-onet_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onet-103">[103]</a></sup> Similar festivities are held in other cities around Poland. </p>
      <p>For those who do not wish to spend the New Year in the city, the mountains are a popular destination. <a href="/wiki/Zakopane" title="Zakopane">Zakopane</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>, is the most popular Polish mountain resort in winter. </p>
      <p>Also, New Year's Eve (<i>Sylwester</i>) celebrations are in <a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Spodek" title="Spodek">Spodek</a> arena. In <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82awatycze" title="Sławatycze">Sławatycze</a>, people tour the streets dressed up as bearded men.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Major television networks broadcast the events live all across the country on New Year's Eve like <a href="/wiki/Polsat" title="Polsat">Polsat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         </div>Madeira

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> the New Year celebration is taken very seriously. The tradition is to drink champagne and eat twelve raisins – one for each month of the year, making a wish for each. Another Portuguese tradition is a special cake called <i><a href="/wiki/Bolo-Rei" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolo-Rei">Bolo-Rei</a></i> (literally: King Cake). <i>Bolo-Rei</i> is a round cake with a large hole in the centre, resembling a crown covered with crystallised and dried fruit. It is baked from a soft, white dough, with raisins, various nuts and crystallised fruit. Inside is hidden the characteristic <i>fava</i> (<a href="/wiki/Broad_bean" class="mw-redirect" title="Broad bean">broad bean</a>). Tradition dictates that whoever finds the <i>fava</i> has to pay for the <i>Bolo-Rei</i> next year. Initially, a small prize (usually a small metal toy) was also included within the cake. However, the inclusion of the prize was forbidden by the European Union for safety reasons. The Portuguese brought the recipe of the <i><a href="/wiki/Gateau_des_Rois" class="mw-redirect" title="Gateau des Rois">Gateau des Rois</a></i> from France in the second half of the 19th century. To this day, this recipe is a very well kept secret. </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> the New Year is celebrated with a grand concert. The New Year's Concert is held at the CCB (<a href="/wiki/Centro_Cultural_de_Bel%C3%A9m" class="mw-redirect" title="Centro Cultural de Belém">Centro Cultural de Belém</a>) on the evening of 1 January, featuring the prestigious Lisbon Metropolitan Orchestra. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanghelion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Vanghelion.jpg/170px-Vanghelion.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Vanghelion.jpg/255px-Vanghelion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Vanghelion.jpg/340px-Vanghelion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanghelion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Romexpo" title="Romexpo">Romexpo</a> indoors during <i>Vanghelion</i> New Year's Eve party.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional celebrations of New Year's Eve (<i>Revelion</i>) are the norm in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>. Romanians follow centuries-old customs, rituals, and conventions. Children sing "<a href="/wiki/Plugu%C8%99orul" title="Plugușorul">Plugușorul</a>" and "Sorcova", traditional carols that wish goodwill, happiness and success. </p>
      <p>Parties are common in the evening. Since the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution_of_1989" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Revolution of 1989">Romanian Revolution of 1989</a>, Romanians have gathered in the <a href="/wiki/University_Square,_Bucharest" title="University Square, Bucharest">University Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>. Other significant parties occur in <a href="/wiki/Pia%C8%9Ba_Constitu%C8%9Biei" title="Piața Constituției">Piața Constituției</a>. New Year's Eve is also marked by a national all-night telecast on <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Television" title="Romanian Television">Romanian Television</a>, which also celebrates its anniversary on this holiday, having opened its doors in the New Year's Eve of 1956. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Novy_God" title="Novy God">Novy God</a>
      </div>
