        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:S_novym_godom_2012.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Midnight at Red Square in 2012.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most prominent public celebration of the New Year is held at <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin_Clock" title="Kremlin Clock">Kremlin Clock</a>—whose chimes at midnight are traditionally followed by the playing of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_national_anthem" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian national anthem">Russian national anthem</a>, and a fireworks display.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President's</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Year_Address_by_President_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="New Year Address by President of Russia">New Year's address</a> is traditionally televised shortly before midnight in each time zone, reflecting on the previous year and the state of the country; in 1999, unpopular president <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> used the New Year's address to announce his resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Secularity" title="Secularity">Secular</a> celebrations of the New Year in Russia, also known as <i>Novy God</i>, are derived from traditions associated with <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>; <a href="/wiki/New_Year_tree" title="New Year tree">New Year trees</a> (<i>yolka</i>) are put up in homes and in public, and <a href="/wiki/Ded_Moroz" title="Ded Moroz">Grandfather Frost</a> (<i>Ded Moroz</i>) delivers presents to children for New Year's Day in a similar manner to <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a>. The practice dates back to the early 20th century: due to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party</a>'s stance of <a href="/wiki/State_atheism" title="State atheism">state atheism</a> and a larger series of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_anti-religious_legislation" title="Soviet anti-religious legislation">anti-religious policies</a>, the celebration of Christmas and other religious holidays was widely discouraged. In particular, <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas trees</a> were singled out for originating from <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> enemy <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and being a symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>. In 1935, Soviet politician <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Postyshev" title="Pavel Postyshev">Pavel Postyshev</a> and other high-ranking officials began to promote the concept of New Year trees as a wide, secular tradition—representing happiness and prosperity among youth. Even with the reinstatement of religious holidays after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Novy God has remained a popular celebration in modern Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Father_Frost_and_the_Snow_Maiden_deliver_Russia's_winter_warmer,_by_Helen_Womack,_31_December_1996_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Father_Frost_and_the_Snow_Maiden_deliver_Russia's_winter_warmer,_by_Helen_Womack,_31_December_1996-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MIG_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIG-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dice2009_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dice2009-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Soviet film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Irony_of_Fate" title="The Irony of Fate">The Irony of Fate</a></i>—which is set during New Year celebrations—is a staple in former Soviet countries. It is often broadcast by Russian television channels on New Year's Eve, to the extent that it has been compared to the traditional broadcast of <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Wonderful_Life" title="It's a Wonderful Life">It's a Wonderful Life</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">Christmas Eve</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-D_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 January, some people celebrate "Old New Year", according to the Julian calendar. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve in Serbia is traditionally celebrated extensively. Indoors, families celebrate New Year's Eve with an abundance of food. Serbs decorate trees, <i>Novogodišnja jelka</i>, at New Year's Eve, rather than at Christmas Eve. Near, or after midnight, Santa Claus (<i>Deda Mraz</i>) visits houses and leaves presents under the tree, to be unpacked then or, if the family is asleep, to be discovered in the morning. </p>
      <p>Serbian New Year's celebrations take place in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, and several other major cities such as <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a>. As of mid-December, cities are extensively decorated and lit. The decorations remain until way into January due to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>. Throughout the region, especially amongst former <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> republics, Belgrade is the most popular destination for major parties. </p>
      <p>On 13 January, a large part of the population<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> celebrates "<a href="/wiki/Old_New_Year" title="Old New Year">Serbian New Year</a>", according to the Julian calendar. Usually, one concert is organized in front of either City Hall or the National Parliament in Belgrade, while fireworks are prepared by the Serbian Orthodox Church and fired from the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Sava" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Saint Sava">Cathedral of Saint Sava</a>, where people also gather. Other cities also organize such celebrations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, New Year's Eve is known as a Saint Sylvester's Day (Silvestrovo). Streets are decorated for December. In larger cities like <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maribor" title="Maribor">Maribor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celje" title="Celje">Celje</a> or <a href="/wiki/Koper" title="Koper">Koper</a> there are concerts, culture programmes and countdowns followed by fireworks. There is also a special programme on national TV. Tradition is that the family comes together and has dinner. At midnight, people toast with champagne, wish each other a happy new year, fortune and health. People have already decorated the Christmas tree before Christmas and children are waiting for the third "Goodman of December – Dedek Mraz." </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg/220px-Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg/330px-Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg/440px-Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nochevieja_puertadelsol_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol" title="Puerta del Sol">Puerta del Sol</a> on New Year's Eve, 2005.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Spanish New Year's Eve (<i>Nochevieja</i> or <i>Fin de Año</i>) celebrations usually begin with a family dinner, traditionally including <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimp</a> or <a href="/wiki/Prawns" class="mw-redirect" title="Prawns">prawns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a> or <a href="/wiki/Capon" title="Capon">capon</a>. The actual countdown is primarily followed from the clock on top of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_House_of_the_Post_Office" title="Royal House of the Post Office">Royal House of the Post Office</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol" title="Puerta del Sol">Puerta del Sol</a> Square in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>. It is traditional to eat <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Grapes" title="Twelve Grapes">Twelve Grapes</a>, one on each chime of the clock. This tradition has its origins in 1909 when grape growers in <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a> thought of it as a way to cut down on the large production surplus they had had that year. Nowadays, the tradition is followed by almost every Spaniard, and the twelve grapes have become synonymous with the New Year. After the clock has finished striking twelve, people greet each other and toast with sparkling wine such as <a href="/wiki/Cava_(Spanish_wine)" title="Cava (Spanish wine)">cava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Champagne_(wine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Champagne (wine)">champagne</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cider" title="Cider">cider</a>. The song "Un año más" by the Spanish group <a href="/wiki/Mecano" title="Mecano">Mecano</a>, is frequently played. The event is broadcast live on major Spanish networks including <a href="/wiki/Antena_3_(Spanish_TV_channel)" title="Antena 3 (Spanish TV channel)">Antena 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radio_y_Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio y Televisión Española">RTVE</a>. </p>
      <p>Earlier in the evening at around 20:00, there is a 10k run called <a href="/wiki/San_Silvestre_Vallecana" title="San Silvestre Vallecana">San Silvestre Vallecana</a>, which starts on <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Castellana" title="Paseo de la Castellana">Paseo de la Castellana</a>, next to <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago Bernabéu Stadium">Santiago Bernabéu Stadium</a>, and ends at the <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_F%C3%BAtbol_de_Vallecas" title="Campo de Fútbol de Vallecas">Vallecas Stadium</a>. Professional runners come to Madrid for this 10k.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After the family dinner and the grapes, many young people attend <i>cotillones de nochevieja</i> parties (named for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> word <i>cotillón</i>, which refers to party supplies like confetti, party blowers, and party hats) at pubs, clubs, and similar places. Parties usually last until the next morning and range from small, personal celebrations at local bars to huge parties with guests numbering the thousands at hotel convention rooms. Early the next morning, party attendees usually gather to have the traditional winter breakfast of hot chocolate and fried pastry (<i>chocolate con <a href="/wiki/Churro" title="Churro">churros</a></i>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg/220px-New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg/330px-New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg/440px-New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1072" data-file-height="712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:New_Years_Eve_2008-2009_-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> fireworks on New Year's Eve, 2008.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, New Year's Eve is usually celebrated with families or with friends. A few hours before and after midnight, people usually party and eat a special dinner, often three courses. New Year's Eve is celebrated with large fireworks displays throughout the country, especially in the cities. People over the age of 18 are allowed to buy fireworks, which are sold by local stores or by private people. While watching or lighting fireworks at midnight, people usually drink champagne. </p>
      <p>The Swedish lottery television show <i><a href="/wiki/BingoLotto" class="mw-redirect" title="BingoLotto">BingoLotto</a></i> features a special New Year's Eve edition to commemorate the holiday with musical guests, four bingo games, and surprises. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, New Year's Eve is typically celebrated in private gatherings or public events. </p>
      <p>The final of the <a href="/wiki/Spengler_Cup" title="Spengler Cup">Spengler Cup</a> ice hockey tournament is traditionally held on New Year's Eve. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv,_2019-2020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg/220px-Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg/330px-Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg/440px-Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv%2C_2019-2020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1064"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Christmas_tree_in_Kyiv,_2019-2020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>New Year celebration in <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, New Year's has the same cultural significance as Christmas has in the United States, but without the religious connotations. Ukrainian families traditionally install spruce trees at home, the equivalent of a Christmas tree. Families gather to eat a large feast and reflect on the past year. They have a large celebration, make toasts, and make wishes for a happy New Year. Families give presents to their friends as well as informal acquaintances. As Ukrainians are traditionally a close-knit community, it is seen as a taboo to not give presents to those the family associates with. Children stay up until midnight, waiting for the New Year. During these celebrations, many Ukrainians tune to special New Year shows, which have become a long-standing tradition for Ukrainian TV. And just before midnight the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a> gives his New Year's message to the nation, and when the clock strikes 12, the National Anthem <a href="/wiki/Shche_ne_vmerla_Ukraina" title="Shche ne vmerla Ukraina">Shche ne vmerla Ukraina</a> is played in all TV and radio stations as well as in <a href="/wiki/Maidan_Nezalezhnosti" title="Maidan Nezalezhnosti">Independence Square</a> in Kyiv and other cities where holiday celebrations are held. </p>
      <p>The first New year dish in Ukraine which associates with the New year for every Ukrainian person is the Olivier salad. It has become the main «character» of many jokes and anecdotes. There are several versions about where the name Olivier comes from, but most people say that it appeared thanks to the French chef Olivier, who lived in the USSR in the 1960s and was the owner of a French restaurant in Moscow. He was the first one to cook this dish. Nowadays this salad is also called Russian, potato and meat salad.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New Year is often considered a "pre-celebration" for Greek Catholics and Eastern Orthodox living in Eastern Europe, primarily in Ukraine, since Christmas is celebrated on 7 January. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="England">England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg/220px-LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg/330px-LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg/440px-LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LondonTrafSQNYE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Thousands of people gather in <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a> for New Year celebrations, including fireworks at the <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a> at midnight.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most prominent New Year's Eve (Old Year's Night) celebration in England is that of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">Central London</a>, where the arrival of midnight is greeted with the chimes of <a href="/wiki/Big_Ben" title="Big Ben">Big Ben</a>. In recent years, <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve_in_London" title="New Year's Eve in London">a major fireworks display</a> has also been held, with fireworks launched from the nearby <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a> Ferris wheel. On New Year's Eve 2010, an estimated 250,000 people gathered to view an eight-minute fireworks display around and above the London Eye which was, for the first time, set to a musical soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The 2020-21 event doesn’t have any spectators because of the COVID-19 pandemic, but instead used a drone and fireworks show. </p>
      <p>Other major New Year events are held in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scotland">Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hogmanay" title="Hogmanay">Hogmanay</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh%27s_Hogmanay" title="Edinburgh's Hogmanay">Edinburgh's Hogmanay</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:EdinburghNYE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/EdinburghNYE.jpg/220px-EdinburghNYE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/EdinburghNYE.jpg/330px-EdinburghNYE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/EdinburghNYE.jpg/440px-EdinburghNYE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2240" data-file-height="1752"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:EdinburghNYE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hogmanay" title="Hogmanay">Hogmanay</a> fireworks in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, New Year's (<i><a href="/wiki/Hogmanay" title="Hogmanay">Hogmanay</a></i>) is celebrated with several different customs, such as <a href="/wiki/First-Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="First-Foot">First-Footing</a>, which involves friends or family members going to each other's houses with a gift of whisky and sometimes a lump of coal. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, the Scottish capital, hosts one of the world's most famous New Year celebrations. The celebration is focused on a major street party along <a href="/wiki/Princes_Street" title="Princes Street">Princes Street</a>. The cannon is fired at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Castle" title="Edinburgh Castle">Edinburgh Castle</a> at the stroke of midnight, followed by a large fireworks display. Edinburgh hosts a festival of four or five days, beginning on 28 December, and lasting until New Year's Day or 2 January, which is also a <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holiday</a> in Scotland. </p>
      <p>Other cities across Scotland, such as <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stirling" title="Stirling">Stirling</a> have large organised celebrations too, including fireworks at midnight. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">BBC Scotland</a> <a href="/wiki/Hogmanay_Live" title="Hogmanay Live">broadcast the celebrations</a> in Edinburgh to a Scottish audience, with the celebrations also screened across the world. <a href="/wiki/STV_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="STV (TV network)">STV</a> covers both worldwide New Year celebrations, and details of events happening around Scotland. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales">Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Calennig" title="Calennig">Calennig</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg/170px-Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg/255px-Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg/340px-Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="947" data-file-height="1311"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mari_Lwyd_NLW.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Mari Lwyd c. 1910–1914. Traditionally carried from door to door during <a href="/wiki/Calennig" title="Calennig">Calennig</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Welsh</a> tradition of giving gifts and money on New Year's Day (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Calennig</i>) is an ancient custom that survives in modern-day Wales, though nowadays it is now customary to give bread and cheese.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Thousands of people descend every year on <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> to enjoy live music, catering, ice-skating, funfairs, and fireworks. Many of the celebrations take place at <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Castle" title="Cardiff Castle">Cardiff Castle</a> and <a href="/wiki/City_Hall,_Cardiff" title="City Hall, Cardiff">Cardiff City Hall</a>. </p>
      <p>Every New Year's Eve, the <a href="/wiki/Nos_Galan_road_race" title="Nos Galan road race">Nos Galan road race</a> (<i>Rasys Nos Galan</i>), a five-kilometre (3.1&nbsp;mi) running contest, is held in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Ash,_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain Ash, Wales">Mountain Ash</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cynon_Valley" title="Cynon Valley">Cynon Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_Cynon_Taf" title="Rhondda Cynon Taf">Rhondda Cynon Taf</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a>. The race celebrates the life and achievements of Welsh runner <a href="/wiki/Guto_Nyth_Br%C3%A2n" title="Guto Nyth Brân">Guto Nyth Brân</a>. </p>
      <p>Founded in 1958 by local runner Bernard Baldwin, it is run over the five-kilometre route of Guto's first competitive race. The main race starts with a church service at <a href="/wiki/Llanwynno" class="mw-redirect" title="Llanwynno">Llanwynno</a>, and then a wreath is laid on Guto's grave in <a href="/wiki/Llanwynno" class="mw-redirect" title="Llanwynno">Llanwynno</a> graveyard. After lighting a torch, it is carried to the nearby town of Mountain Ash, where the main race takes place. </p>
      <p>The race consists of a double circuit of the town centre, starting in Henry Street and ending in Oxford Street, by the commemorative statue of Guto. Traditionally, the race was timed to end at midnight, but in recent times it was rescheduled for the convenience of family entertainment, now concluding at around 9<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>pm. </p>
      <p>This has resulted in a growth in size and scale, and the proceedings now start with an afternoon of street entertainment, and fun run races for children, concluding with the church service, elite runners' race, and presentations. </p> 
      <h2><span id="Middle_East_.26_North_Africa"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East_&amp;_North_Africa">Middle East &amp; North Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Middle East &amp; North Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Algeria">Algeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Algeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, New Year's Eve (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Réveillon</i>; <i><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">Ra’s al-‘Ām</span>‎</i>) is usually celebrated with family and friends. In the largest cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif" title="Sétif">Sétif</a>, and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9ja%C3%AFa" title="Béjaïa">Béjaïa</a>, there are large celebrations which may feature concerts, late-night partying, firecrackers, fireworks at midnight and sparklers and shouts of "<i>Bonne année&nbsp;!</i>". The <a href="/wiki/Martyrs%27_Memorial,_Algiers" title="Martyrs' Memorial, Algiers">Martyrs' Memorial</a> and the Grand-Post Place in Algiers are the main attraction for the majority of <a href="/wiki/Algerians" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerians">Algerians</a> during the celebration, while some others prefer spending this special night outside the country, generally in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. </p>
      <p>At 8pm <span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Time_in_Algeria" title="Time in Algeria">AST</a>)</span>, the President's message of greetings to Algerians is read on TV. The <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tablissement_public_de_t%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision" class="mw-redirect" title="Établissement public de télévision">EPTV</a> network airs a yearly New Year's Eve entertainment show, variying its name, hosts and guests, which features sketches and musical performances. Popular films are also broadcast. At home or at restaurants, a special type of pastry cake called "<i>la bûche</i>" is eaten, and black coffee or soda is often drunk with it. People eat it a few minutes before the New Year's countdown. </p>
      <p>On <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a> (<i>le jour de l'an</i>), people, especially children, write their "New Year's letter" on decorated paper, called "<i>Carte de bonne année</i>", to their parents and relatives, featuring their <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_resolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="New Year's resolutions">resolutions</a> and wishes. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Egypt the new year is celebrated with fireworks and often evening parties. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>New Year's Eve (<i>Silvester</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, is celebrated informally among some groups, by parties, social get togethers, concerts, and dining out in major cities such as <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>. Immigrants from the former <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> celebrate <a href="/wiki/Novy_God" title="Novy God">Novy God</a>, the Russian version of the holiday. The Eve of the Jewish New Year (<i>Erev Rosh Hashanah</i>) is also observed on the 29th of <a href="/wiki/Elul" title="Elul">Elul</a> according to the Jewish calendar (falling sometime in September or October by the Gregorian calendar).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon_and_Syria">Lebanon and Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Lebanon and Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, people celebrate New Year's Eve with a dinner attended by family and friends. The dinner features traditional dishes such as tabouli, hummus, kibbi, and other Syrian and Lebanese foods. These celebrations could also take place in restaurants and clubs. Game shows are also organized where people can try to win money. The countdown to New Year's is broadcast through the leading TV channel and the celebrations usually continue until sunrise. Fireworks are lit throughout the night. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morocco">Morocco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Morocco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CasablancaFire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/CasablancaFire.jpg/220px-CasablancaFire.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/CasablancaFire.jpg/330px-CasablancaFire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/CasablancaFire.jpg/440px-CasablancaFire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="357"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CasablancaFire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> fireworks display
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, New Year's Eve (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">رأس العام</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Rass l'aam</i>—"head of the year") is celebrated in the company of family and friends. People get together to eat cake, dance, and laugh. Traditionally, people celebrate it at home, but some prefer to go to nightclubs. At midnight, fireworks are displayed across <a href="/wiki/Ain_Diab" title="Ain Diab">Ain Diab</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Corniche" title="Corniche">corniche</a> of Casablanca. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calendar" title="Islamic calendar">Islamic calendar</a> is the traditional religious calendar, the <a href="/wiki/Committee_for_the_Promotion_of_Virtue_and_the_Prevention_of_Vice_(Saudi_Arabia)" title="Committee for the Promotion of Virtue and the Prevention of Vice (Saudi Arabia)">Committee for the Promotion of Virtue and the Prevention of Vice</a>—Saudi Arabia's <a href="/wiki/Islamic_religious_police" title="Islamic religious police">religious police</a>, has enforced a ban on public festivities of the Gregorian New Year. The organization can also fine shops for offering New Year's-related products, and confiscate them. However, the organization does not go after individual citizens holding private celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-emirates247-saudinewyear_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emirates247-saudinewyear-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aljaz-saudinye_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz-saudinye-120">[120]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg/220px-Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg/330px-Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg/440px-Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2305" data-file-height="3072"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>New Year's Eve decorations in <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kadıköy">Kadıköy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Numerous decorations and customs traditionally associated with Christmas and <a href="/wiki/Bayram_(Turkey)" title="Bayram (Turkey)">Bayrams</a> are part of <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a> New Year's Eve celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. Homes and streets are lit in glittering lights. Small gifts are exchanged, and large family dinners are organized with family and friends, featuring a special <a href="/wiki/Stuffed_turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuffed turkey">turkey</a> dish stuffed with a <a href="/wiki/Zante_currant" title="Zante currant">zante currant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pine_nuts" class="mw-redirect" title="Pine nuts">pine nuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pimiento" title="Pimiento">pimiento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dill" title="Dill">dill</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pilaf" title="Pilaf">iç pilav</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Dolma" title="Dolma">dolma</a>, hot <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6rek" title="Börek">börek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">baklava</a>, and various other <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish dishes</a>; accompanied with <a href="/wiki/Rak%C4%B1" title="Rakı">rakı</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_wine" title="Turkish wine">Turkish wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boza" title="Boza">boza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharbat" title="Sharbat"><i>şerbet</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Salep" title="Salep">salep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_tea" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish tea">Turkish tea</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Turkish_coffee" title="Turkish coffee">coffee</a>. Even though Turkish people generally do not celebrate <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, decorating <a href="/wiki/New_Year_tree" title="New Year tree">New Year trees</a> is an emerging tradition on New Year's Eve in Turkey and the Turks associate <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a> with New Year's Eve. </p>
      <p>Television and radio channels are known to continuously broadcast a variety of special New Year's Eve programs, while <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a> all around the country organize fundraising events for the poor, in addition to celebratory public shows such as concerts and family-friendly events, as well as more traditional forms of entertainment such as the <a href="/wiki/Karag%C3%B6z_and_Hacivat" title="Karagöz and Hacivat">Karagöz and Hacivat</a> <a href="/wiki/Shadow_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Shadow theatre">shadow-theater</a>, and even performances by the <a href="/wiki/Mehter" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehter">Mehter</a>—the <a href="/wiki/Janissary" title="Janissary">Janissary</a> Band that was founded during the days of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. </p>
      <p>Public and private parties with large public attendances are organised in a number of cities and towns, particularly in the largest metropolitan areas such as <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Izmir" class="mw-redirect" title="Izmir">Izmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adana" title="Adana">Adana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bursa" title="Bursa">Bursa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antalya" title="Antalya">Antalya</a>, with the biggest celebrations taking place in Istanbul's <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyoğlu">Beyoğlu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1" title="Nişantaşı">Nişantaşı</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kadıköy">Kadıköy</a> districts and Ankara's <a href="/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square" title="Kızılay Square">Kızılay Square</a>, which generally feature dancing, concerts, laser and light shows as well as the traditional countdown and fireworks display. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Arab_Emirates">United Arab Emirates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: United Arab Emirates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a>—the world's tallest building—has hosted an annual fireworks display, which is among the world's most expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> A fireworks show was not held for 2017–18: instead, a multimedia <a href="/wiki/Son_et_lumi%C3%A8re_(show)" title="Son et lumière (show)">light and sound show</a> was presented using the tower's lighting system, which set a <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Record</a> for the largest light and sound show staged on a single building.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The fireworks show returned for 2019, in tandem with a multimedia presentation.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg/220px-Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg/330px-Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg/440px-Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_khalifa_opening_ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>New year celebrations, including fireworks at the <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> at midnight
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG/220px-Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG/330px-Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG/440px-Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3017" data-file-height="2236"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_new_years_2008-9.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sydney New Year's Eve 2008–09
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Each major city in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> holds New Year's Eve celebrations, usually accompanied by a fireworks display and other events. The most prominent celebration in the country is <a href="/wiki/Sydney_New_Year%27s_Eve" title="Sydney New Year's Eve">Sydney New Year's Eve</a>, which takes place at <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydney Harbour">Sydney Harbour</a> and consists of two fireworks shows — the evening "Family Fireworks" held at 9:00&nbsp;p.m., followed by the main fireworks at midnight. <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour_Bridge" title="Sydney Harbour Bridge">Sydney Harbour Bridge</a> is a focal point of the show, via pyrotechnics launched from the bridge, as well as lighting displays that illuminate it during the show—colloquially known as the "bridge effect", and previously taking the form of a symbol, installed on its trusses, that reflected an annual theme.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Park,_Perth" title="Gloucester Park, Perth">Gloucester Park</a>, a racecourse in central <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Western_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Perth, Western Australia">Perth</a>, is the largest and most recognized display in the Western Australian city. In <a href="/wiki/Brisbane,_Queensland" class="mw-redirect" title="Brisbane, Queensland">Brisbane</a> events are held at <a href="/wiki/South_Bank,_Queensland" title="South Bank, Queensland">Southbank</a>. At night, 50,000 people gather at sites around the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a> to watch a fireworks display. In <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, hundreds of thousands of people come to the Central Business District to see the fireworks.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In the South Australian capital of <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>, events are held at both <a href="/wiki/Rymill_Park" title="Rymill Park">Rymill Park</a> in the city and at <a href="/wiki/Glenelg,_South_Australia" title="Glenelg, South Australia">Glenelg</a> beach. </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_(rainbow_fireworks).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg/650px-Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="650" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg/975px-Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg/1300px-Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_%28rainbow_fireworks%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="659"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_New_Years_Eve_celebrations_2018_(rainbow_fireworks).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div><a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> New Year's Eve celebrations 2018
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kiribati">Kiribati</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Kiribati">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B14" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+14">UTC+14</a>) part of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> (and other Kiribati's <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>, especially populated <a href="/wiki/Tabuaeran" title="Tabuaeran">Tabuaeran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teraina" title="Teraina">Teraina</a>), is one of the first locations in the world to welcome the New Year. Other Kiribati islands follow at <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B13" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+13">UTC+13</a> and <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B12" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+12">UTC+12</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Many of New Zealand's cities and towns see in the new year with open-air concerts and fireworks displays. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> regularly has a fireworks display at midnight from the top of the <a href="/wiki/Sky_Tower_(Auckland)" title="Sky Tower (Auckland)">Sky Tower</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Kitts_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Frank Kitts Park">Frank Kitts Park</a> is the venue for a festival including fireworks, music, and open-air film displays. Similar events occur in Hamilton, starting with a family-friendly event at Steele Park, followed by an adult-specific party at <a href="/wiki/SkyCity_Hamilton" class="mw-redirect" title="SkyCity Hamilton">SkyCity Hamilton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gisborne,_New_Zealand" title="Gisborne, New Zealand">Gisborne</a>, one of the first cities in the world to see sunrise at new year<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> also celebrates with a new year festival. The small town of <a href="/wiki/Whangamata" class="mw-redirect" title="Whangamata">Whangamata</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Coromandel_Peninsula" title="Coromandel Peninsula">Coromandel Peninsula</a>, is a major party venue in the new year, especially for Aucklanders. </p>
      <p>In the South Island, both <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dunedin" title="Dunedin">Dunedin</a> host free live music concerts culminating with a midnight fireworks display. These are held at <a href="/wiki/Hagley_Park,_Christchurch" title="Hagley Park, Christchurch">Hagley Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Octagon,_Dunedin" title="The Octagon, Dunedin">The Octagon</a> respectively. The South Island's main resort town, <a href="/wiki/Queenstown,_New_Zealand" title="Queenstown, New Zealand">Queenstown</a> is also a major new year party venue, with music and fireworks. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Samoa">Samoa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Samoa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Since changing the <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zone</a> from <a href="/wiki/UTC-11" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC-11">UTC-11</a> to <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B13" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+13">UTC+13</a> in winter and <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B14" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+14">UTC+14</a> in summer (including new year), Samoa is the first country to receive the New Year as a whole, sharing it with some parts of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg/300px-John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="478" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg/450px-John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg/600px-John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3352" data-file-height="5336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:John_Masey_Wright_-_John_Rogers_-_Robert_Burns_-_Auld_Lang_Syne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/John_Masey_Wright" title="John Masey Wright">John Masey Wright</a> and John Rogers' c. 1841 illustration of "<a href="/wiki/Auld_Lang_Syne" title="Auld Lang Syne">Auld Lang Syne</a>".
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Music associated with New Year's Eve comes in both classical and popular genres, and there is also <a href="/wiki/Christmas_music" title="Christmas music">Christmas song</a> focus on the arrival of a new year during the <a href="/wiki/Christmas_and_holiday_season" title="Christmas and holiday season">Christmas and holiday season</a>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Auld_Lang_Syne" title="Auld Lang Syne">Auld Lang Syne</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Burns" title="Robert Burns">Robert Burns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a>, in the <i><a href="/wiki/Orgelb%C3%BCchlein" title="Orgelbüchlein">Orgelbüchlein</a></i>, composed three chorale preludes for the new year: <i>Helft mir Gotts Güte preisen</i> ["Help me to praise God's goodness"] (BWV 613); <i>Das alte Jahr vergangen ist</i> ["The old year has passed"] (BWV 614); and <i>In dir ist freude</i> ["In you is joy"] (BWV 615).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>"The year is gone, beyond recall" is a traditional Christian hymn to give thanks for the new year, dating back to 1713.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Happy_New_Year_(song)" title="Happy New Year (song)">Happy New Year</a>" by <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>" by <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/It_Was_a_Very_Good_Year" title="It Was a Very Good Year">It Was a Very Good Year</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Just_Another_New_Year%27s_Eve" title="It's Just Another New Year's Eve">It's Just Another New Year's Eve</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Barry_Manilow" title="Barry Manilow">Barry Manilow</a></li> 
       <li>"Let's Start the New Year Right" by <a href="/wiki/Bing_Crosby" title="Bing Crosby">Bing Crosby</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Celebration_(Kool_%26_the_Gang_song)" title="Celebration (Kool &amp; the Gang song)">Celebration</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Kool_%26_the_Gang" title="Kool &amp; the Gang">Kool &amp; the Gang</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day_(U2_song)" title="New Year's Day (U2 song)">New Year's Day</a>" by <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/The_Final_Countdown_(song)" title="The Final Countdown (song)">The Final Countdown</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Europe_(band)" title="Europe (band)">Europe</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Ding_Dong_Ding_Dong" class="mw-redirect" title="Ding Dong Ding Dong">Ding Dong Ding Dong</a>" by <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Same_Old_Lang_Syne" title="Same Old Lang Syne">Same Old Lang Syne</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Fogelberg" title="Dan Fogelberg">Dan Fogelberg</a></li> 
       <li>"Let's Spend This New Year's Eve At Home" by Christi Bauerlee</li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Good_Riddance_(Time_of_Your_Life)" title="Good Riddance (Time of Your Life)">Good Riddance (Time of Your Life)</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a></li> 
       <li>"Kiss Me at Midnight" by <a href="/wiki/%27N_Sync" class="mw-redirect" title="'N Sync">'N Sync</a> from their 1998 album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Winter_Album_(N_Sync_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Winter Album (N Sync album)">The Winter Album</a></i></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Firework_(song)" title="Firework (song)">Firework</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a></li> 
       <li>"This Is the New Year" by <a href="/wiki/A_Great_Big_World" title="A Great Big World">A Great Big World</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day_(Taylor_Swift_song)" title="New Year's Day (Taylor Swift song)">New Year's Day</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/1999_(Prince_song)" title="1999 (Prince song)">1999</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Willennium" title="Willennium">Will 2K</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Millennium_(song)" title="Millennium (song)">Millennium</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Brand_New_Day_(Sting_song)" title="Brand New Day (Sting song)">Brand New Day</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a></li> 
       <li>"<a href="/wiki/Disco_2000_(song)" title="Disco 2000 (song)">Disco 2000</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(band)" title="Pulp (band)">Pulp</a></li> 
       <li>"Año Más" by <a href="/wiki/Mecano" title="Mecano">Mecano</a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Year%27s_Eve&amp;action=edit&amp;section=89" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

         <li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bangladesh celebrates New Year in ships and yachts</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Muslim Republican of Bangladesh prays to Allah for a fruitful year</span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gisborne is further east than any other New Zealand city, but due to the earth's axial tilt, the hills around Dunedin also receive sunrise at an almost identical time at new year. Nuku'alofa in Tonga and Apia and Samoa also receive the sun at almost exactly the same time. Given that the earth's axial tilt oscillates fractionally, the title of "the first city to see the sun" — though usually claimed by Gisborne — is open to some debate.</span> </li>
